margin-left: 0; text-align:left;display:none; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Alec_Shelbrooke" and the Humber</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.leeds.gov.uk/">www.leeds.gov.uk</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Leeds</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/i\xcb\x90/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">i\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-Leeds.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/En-uk-Leeds.ogg" class="internal" title="En-uk-Leeds.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> in the county of <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a>, England.\n</p><p>Leeds was a small manorial borough in the 13th century, and in the 17th and 18th centuries it became a major centre for the production and trading of wool, and in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> a major <a href="/wiki/Mill_town" title="Mill town">mill town</a>; wool was still the dominant industry, but <a href="/wiki/Flax" title="Flax">flax</a>, engineering, iron <a href="/wiki/Foundry" title="Foundry">foundries</a>, printing, and other industries were also important.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> From being a market town in the valley of the <a href="/wiki/River_Aire" title="River Aire">River Aire</a> in the 16th century, Leeds expanded and absorbed the surrounding villages to become a populous urban centre by the mid-20th century. It now lies within the United Kingdom\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Europe" title="List of metropolitan areas in Europe">fourth-most populous urban area</a>, with a population of 2.6&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds has one of the most diverse economies of the all the UK\xe2\x80\x99s main employment centres and has seen the fastest rate of private-sector jobs growth of any UK city. It also has the highest ratio of private to public sector jobs of all the UK\'s Core Cities, with 77% of its workforce working in the private sector. Leeds has the third-largest jobs total by local authority area, with 480,000 in employment and self-employment at the beginning of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-leeds.gov.uk_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeds.gov.uk-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Leeds is ranked as a <a href="/wiki/Global_city#GaWC_study" title="Global city">gamma world city</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">Globalization and World Cities Research Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TheWorld_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheWorld-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Leeds is the cultural, financial and commercial heart of the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Urban_Area" title="West Yorkshire Urban Area">West Yorkshire Urban Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Leeds is served by four universities, and has the fourth largest student population in the country and the country\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_UK_cities_by_GVA" title="List of UK cities by GVA">fourth largest urban economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BrookingsMetroEconomy_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BrookingsMetroEconomy-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, Leeds has become the largest legal and financial centre, outside London<sup id="cite_ref-leeds.gov.uk_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeds.gov.uk-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> with the financial and insurance services industry worth \xc2\xa313&#160;billion to the city\'s economy. The Finance and business service sector account for 38% of total output<sup id="cite_ref-leeds.gov.uk_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeds.gov.uk-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-investleedscityregion.com_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investleedscityregion.com-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> with more than 30 national and international banks located in the city, including an office of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Leeds is also the UK\'s third-largest manufacturing centre with around 1,800 firms and 39,000 employees, Leeds manufacturing firms account for 8.8% of total employment in the city and is worth over \xc2\xa37 billion to the local economy.<sup id="cite_ref-investleedscityregion.com_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investleedscityregion.com-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The largest sub-sectors are engineering, printing and publishing, food and drink, chemicals and medical technology.<sup id="cite_ref-Leeds_2013_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leeds_2013-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Other key sectors include retail, leisure and the visitor economy, construction, and the creative and digital industries. The city saw several firsts, including the oldest-surviving film in existence, <i><a href="/wiki/Roundhay_Garden_Scene" title="Roundhay Garden Scene">Roundhay Garden Scene</a></i> (1888), and the 1767 invention of <a href="/wiki/Soda_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Soda water">soda water</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Public transport, rail and road communications networks in the region are focused on Leeds, and the second phase of <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> will connect it to London via <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Hub_railway_station" title="East Midlands Hub railway station">East Midlands Hub</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_Interchange" title="Meadowhall Interchange">Sheffield Meadowhall</a>. Leeds currently has the third busiest <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">train station</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and the tenth busiest <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bradford_Airport" title="Leeds Bradford Airport">airport</a> outside <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" class="toctext">Governance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Public_sector"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Public sector</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Shopping"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Shopping</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Landmarks"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Landmarks</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Recreation"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Recreation</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Walking"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Walking</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Parks_and_open_spaces"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Parks and open spaces</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Schools"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Schools</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Further_and_higher_education"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Further and higher education</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Art"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Art</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Carnivals_and_festivals"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Carnivals and festivals</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Cinema"><span class="tocnumber">10.3</span> <span class="toctext">Cinema</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">10.4</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Museums"><span class="tocnumber">10.5</span> <span class="toctext">Museums</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Music,_theatre_and_dance"><span class="tocnumber">10.6</span> <span class="toctext">Music, theatre and dance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Nightlife"><span class="tocnumber">10.7</span> <span class="toctext">Nightlife</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Leeds_teams"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Leeds teams</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Public_services"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Public services</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#References_and_notes"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">References and notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Leeds" title="History of Leeds">History of Leeds</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The name derives from the old <a href="/wiki/Common_Brittonic" title="Common Brittonic">Brythonic</a> word <i>Ladenses</i> meaning "people of the fast-flowing river", in reference to the <a href="/wiki/River_Aire" title="River Aire">River Aire</a> that flows through the city.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> This name originally referred to the forested area covering most of the <a href="/wiki/Elmet" title="Elmet">Brythonic kingdom of Elmet</a>, which existed during the 5th century into the early 7th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Fletcher_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fletcher-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bede" title="Bede">Bede</a> states in the fourteenth chapter of his <i><a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_History_of_the_English_People" title="Ecclesiastical History of the English People">Ecclesiastical History</a></i>, in a discussion of an altar surviving from a church erected by <a href="/wiki/Edwin_of_Northumbria" title="Edwin of Northumbria">Edwin of Northumbria</a>, that it is located in <i>...regione quae vocatur Loidis</i> (Latin, "the region which is called Loidis"). An inhabitant of Leeds is locally known as a <i><a href="/wiki/Loiner" title="Loiner">Loiner</a></i>, a word of uncertain origin.<sup id="cite_ref-loiner_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loiner-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The term <i>Leodensian</i> is also used, from the city\'s Latin name.\n</p><p>The name has also been explained as a derivative of <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> <i>lloed</i>, meaning simply "a place".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_development">Economic development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Economic development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Mint,_Granary_Wharf,_Leeds_(5385775582).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/The_Mint%2C_Granary_Wharf%2C_Leeds_%285385775582%29.jpg/220px-The_Mint%2C_Granary_Wharf%2C_Leeds_%285385775582%29.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/The_Mint%2C_Granary_Wharf%2C_Leeds_%285385775582%29.jpg/330px-The_Mint%2C_Granary_Wharf%2C_Leeds_%285385775582%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/The_Mint%2C_Granary_Wharf%2C_Leeds_%285385775582%29.jpg/440px-The_Mint%2C_Granary_Wharf%2C_Leeds_%285385775582%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="3750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Mint,_Granary_Wharf,_Leeds_(5385775582).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Liverpool_Canal" title="Leeds and Liverpool Canal">Leeds and Liverpool Canal</a> at <a href="/wiki/Granary_Wharf" title="Granary Wharf">Granary Wharf</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inside_the_Corn_Exchange_2_-_Leeds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Inside_the_Corn_Exchange_2_-_Leeds.jpg/220px-Inside_the_Corn_Exchange_2_-_Leeds.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Inside_the_Corn_Exchange_2_-_Leeds.jpg/330px-Inside_the_Corn_Exchange_2_-_Leeds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Inside_the_Corn_Exchange_2_-_Leeds.jpg/440px-Inside_the_Corn_Exchange_2_-_Leeds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2956" data-file-height="1949" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inside_the_Corn_Exchange_2_-_Leeds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Corn_Exchange" title="Leeds Corn Exchange">Leeds Corn Exchange</a> opened in 1864</div></div></div>\n<p>Leeds developed as a <a href="/wiki/Market_town" title="Market town">market town</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> as part of the local agricultural economy. Before the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, it became a co-ordination centre for the manufacture of woollen cloth, and white <a href="/wiki/Broadcloth" title="Broadcloth">broadcloth</a> was traded at its <a href="/wiki/1st_White_Cloth_Hall" title="1st White Cloth Hall">White Cloth Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cloth_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cloth-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds handled one sixth of England\'s export trade in 1770.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Growth, initially in textiles, was accelerated by the building of the <a href="/wiki/Aire_and_Calder_Navigation" title="Aire and Calder Navigation">Aire and Calder Navigation</a> in 1699 and the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Liverpool_Canal" title="Leeds and Liverpool Canal">Leeds and Liverpool Canal</a> in 1816.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The railway network constructed around Leeds, starting with the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Selby_Railway" title="Leeds and Selby Railway">Leeds and Selby Railway</a> in 1834, provided improved communications with national markets and, significantly for its development, an east-west connection with <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and the ports of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a> giving improved access to international markets.<sup id="cite_ref-transport_geo_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transport_geo-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Alongside technological advances and industrial expansion, Leeds retained an interest in trading in agricultural commodities, with the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Corn_Exchange" title="Leeds Corn Exchange">Corn Exchange</a> opening in 1864.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Rhodes_-_Leeds_from_the_Meadows.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Joseph_Rhodes_-_Leeds_from_the_Meadows.jpg/220px-Joseph_Rhodes_-_Leeds_from_the_Meadows.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Joseph_Rhodes_-_Leeds_from_the_Meadows.jpg/330px-Joseph_Rhodes_-_Leeds_from_the_Meadows.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Joseph_Rhodes_-_Leeds_from_the_Meadows.jpg/440px-Joseph_Rhodes_-_Leeds_from_the_Meadows.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1498" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Rhodes_-_Leeds_from_the_Meadows.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Leeds from the Meadows</i> by Joseph Rhodes, 1825.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Marshall%27s_Mill" title="Marshall&#39;s Mill">Marshall\'s Mill</a> was one of the first of many factories constructed in Leeds from around 1790 when the most significant were woollen finishing and flax mills.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraser_1982_144_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraser_1982_144-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Manufacturing diversified by 1914 to printing, engineering, chemicals and clothing manufacture.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Decline in manufacturing during the 1930s was temporarily reversed by a switch to producing military uniforms and munitions during World War II. However, by the 1970s, the clothing industry was in irreversible decline, facing cheap foreign competition.<sup id="cite_ref-suit_leeds_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suit_leeds-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The contemporary economy has been shaped by <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Council" title="Leeds City Council">Leeds City Council</a>\'s vision of building a \'24-hour European city\' and \'capital of the north\'.<sup id="cite_ref-imagine_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imagine-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The city has developed from the decay of the post-industrial era to become a telephone banking centre, connected to the electronic infrastructure of the modern global economy.<sup id="cite_ref-imagine_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imagine-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> There has been growth in the corporate and legal sectors,<sup id="cite_ref-legal_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legal-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and increased local affluence has led to an expanding retail sector, including the <a href="/wiki/Luxury_goods" title="Luxury goods">luxury goods</a> market.<sup id="cite_ref-retail_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retail-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Region" title="Leeds City Region">Leeds City Region Enterprise Zone</a> was launched in April 2012 to promote development in four sites along the <a href="/wiki/A63_road" title="A63 road">A63</a> East Leeds Link Road.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_local_government_in_Yorkshire" title="History of local government in Yorkshire">History of local government in Yorkshire</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:left; font-size:85%; margin-left:10px; margin-right:10px; margin-top:0px;">\n<caption><b>Leeds (parish) population</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">1881\n</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;">160,109\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">1891\n</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;">177,523\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">1901\n</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;">177,920\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">1911\n</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;">259,394\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">1921\n</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;">269,665\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">1931\n</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;">482,809\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">1941\n</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;">war*\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">1951\n</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;">505,219\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;">1961\n</th>\n<td style="text-align:center;">510,676\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="font-size:smaller" colspan="2">*no census was held due to war\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="font-size:smaller; text-align:center;">source: <a href="/wiki/Census#United_Kingdom" title="Census">UK census</a><sup id="cite_ref-population_parish_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population_parish-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Leeds was a manor and township in the large ancient parish of <i>Leeds St Peter</i>, in the <a href="/wiki/Skyrack" title="Skyrack">Skyrack</a> <a href="/wiki/Hundred_(county_division)" title="Hundred (county division)">wapentake</a> of the <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="West Riding of Yorkshire">West Riding</a> of <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vision_parish_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vision_parish-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Borough of Leeds was created in 1207, when Maurice Paynel, lord of the manor, granted a charter to a small area of the manor, close to the river crossing, in what is now the city centre. Four centuries later, the inhabitants petitioned <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a> for a charter of incorporation, which was granted in 1626. The new charter incorporated the entire parish, including all eleven townships, as the <a href="/wiki/County_Borough_of_Leeds" title="County Borough of Leeds">Borough of Leeds</a> and withdrew the earlier charter. <a href="/wiki/Improvement_commissioners" title="Improvement commissioners">Improvement commissioners</a> were set up in 1755 for paving, lighting, and cleansing of the main streets, including <a href="/wiki/Briggate,_Leeds" title="Briggate, Leeds">Briggate</a> and further powers were added in 1790 to improve the water supply.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_Town_Hall,_General_Election_results.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Leeds_Town_Hall%2C_General_Election_results.jpg/220px-Leeds_Town_Hall%2C_General_Election_results.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Leeds_Town_Hall%2C_General_Election_results.jpg/330px-Leeds_Town_Hall%2C_General_Election_results.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Leeds_Town_Hall%2C_General_Election_results.jpg/440px-Leeds_Town_Hall%2C_General_Election_results.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_Town_Hall,_General_Election_results.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A crowd gathers outside Leeds Town Hall during the 1880 general elections.</div></div></div>\n<p>The borough corporation was reformed under the provisions of <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporations_Act_1835" title="Municipal Corporations Act 1835">Municipal Corporations Act 1835</a>. <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Police" title="Leeds City Police">Leeds Borough Police</a> force was formed in 1836, and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Town_Hall" title="Leeds Town Hall">Leeds Town Hall</a> was completed by the corporation in 1858. In 1866, Leeds and each of the other townships in the borough became <a href="/wiki/Civil_parish" title="Civil parish">civil parishs</a>. The borough became a <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> in 1889, giving it independence from the newly formed West Riding County Council and it gained <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status</a> in 1893. In 1904 the Leeds parish absorbed <a href="/wiki/Beeston,_Leeds" title="Beeston, Leeds">Beeston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Allerton" title="Chapel Allerton">Chapel Allerton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farnley,_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Farnley, West Yorkshire">Farnley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Headingley_cum_Burley" class="mw-redirect" title="Headingley cum Burley">Headingley cum Burley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Potternewton" title="Potternewton">Potternewton</a> from within the borough. In the twentieth century the county borough initiated a series of significant territorial expansions, growing from 21,593 acres (87.38&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) in 1911 to 40,612 acres (164.35&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-vision_cb_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vision_cb-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In 1912 the parish and county borough of Leeds absorbed <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rural_District" title="Leeds Rural District">Leeds Rural District</a>, consisting of the parishes of <a href="/wiki/Roundhay" title="Roundhay">Roundhay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seacroft" title="Seacroft">Seacroft</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Shadwell,_West_Yorkshire" title="Shadwell, West Yorkshire">Shadwell</a>, which had been part of Wetherby Rural District. On 1 April 1925, the parish of Leeds was expanded to cover the whole borough.<sup id="cite_ref-vision_parish_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vision_parish-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The county borough was abolished on 1 April 1974, and its former area was combined with that of the municipal boroughs of <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Borough_of_Morley" title="Municipal Borough of Morley">Morley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Borough_of_Pudsey" title="Municipal Borough of Pudsey">Pudsey</a>; the urban districts of <a href="/wiki/Aireborough" title="Aireborough">Aireborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horsforth" title="Horsforth">Horsforth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otley" title="Otley">Otley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garforth" title="Garforth">Garforth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rothwell,_West_Yorkshire" title="Rothwell, West Yorkshire">Rothwell</a>; and parts of the rural districts of <a href="/wiki/Tadcaster_Rural_District" title="Tadcaster Rural District">Tadcaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wetherby_Rural_District" title="Wetherby Rural District">Wetherby</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wharfedale_Rural_District" title="Wharfedale Rural District">Wharfedale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> This area formed a metropolitan district in the county of <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a>. It gained both borough and city status and is known as the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Leeds" title="City of Leeds">City of Leeds</a>. Initially, local government services were provided by <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Council" title="Leeds City Council">Leeds City Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_County_Council" title="West Yorkshire County Council">West Yorkshire County Council</a>. When the county council was abolished in 1986, the city council absorbed its functions, and some powers passed to organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Metro" title="West Yorkshire Metro">West Yorkshire Passenger Transport Authority</a>. From 1988 two run-down and derelict areas close to the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_city_centre" title="Leeds city centre">city centre</a> were designated for regeneration and became the responsibility of <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Development_Corporation" title="Leeds Development Corporation">Leeds Development Corporation</a>, outside the planning remit of the city council.<sup id="cite_ref-leeds_dc_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeds_dc-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Planning powers were restored to the local authority in 1995 when the development corporation was wound up.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suburban_growth">Suburban growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Suburban growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_1866_by_J_Bartholemew_edited.jpg" class="image"><img alt="This map shows central Leeds and (clockwise from top left) the developing suburbs of Hyde Park, Woodhouse, Sheepscar, New Leeds, Cross Green, Hunslet, Holbeck, Wortley, Armley and Burley." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Leeds_1866_by_J_Bartholemew_edited.jpg/220px-Leeds_1866_by_J_Bartholemew_edited.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Leeds_1866_by_J_Bartholemew_edited.jpg/330px-Leeds_1866_by_J_Bartholemew_edited.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Leeds_1866_by_J_Bartholemew_edited.jpg/440px-Leeds_1866_by_J_Bartholemew_edited.jpg 2x" data-file-width="838" data-file-height="627" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_1866_by_J_Bartholemew_edited.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1866 map of Leeds</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:James_Valentine_The_Briggate_Leeds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/James_Valentine_The_Briggate_Leeds.jpg/220px-James_Valentine_The_Briggate_Leeds.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/James_Valentine_The_Briggate_Leeds.jpg/330px-James_Valentine_The_Briggate_Leeds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/James_Valentine_The_Briggate_Leeds.jpg/440px-James_Valentine_The_Briggate_Leeds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="609" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:James_Valentine_The_Briggate_Leeds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>19th century <a href="/wiki/Briggate,_Leeds" title="Briggate, Leeds">Briggate, Leeds</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1801, 42% of the population of Leeds lived outside the township, in the wider borough. <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">Cholera</a> outbreaks in 1832 and 1849 caused the authorities to address the problems of drainage, sanitation, and water supply. Water was pumped from the River Wharfe, but by 1860 it was too heavily polluted to be usable. Following the Leeds Waterworks Act of 1867 three reservoirs were built at Lindley Wood, Swinsty, and Fewston in the Washburn Valley north of Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Residential growth occurred in Holbeck and Hunslet from 1801 to 1851, but, as these townships became industrialised new areas were favoured for middle class housing.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Land south of the river was developed primarily for industry and secondarily for <a href="/wiki/Back-to-back_house" title="Back-to-back house">back-to-back</a> workers\' dwellings. The Leeds Improvement Act 1866 sought to improve the quality of working class housing by restricting the number of homes that could be built in a single terrace.<sup id="cite_ref-discover_house_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-discover_house-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Holbeck and Leeds formed a continuous built-up area by 1858, with Hunslet nearly meeting them.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraser_1982_98_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraser_1982_98-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In the latter half of the nineteenth century, population growth in Hunslet, Armley, and Wortley outstripped that of Leeds. When pollution became a problem, the wealthier residents left the industrial conurbation to live in Headingley, Potternewton and Chapel Allerton which led to a 50% increase in the population of Headingley and Burley from 1851 to 1861. The middle-class flight from the industrial areas led to development beyond the borough at Roundhay and Adel.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraser_1982_98_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraser_1982_98-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Tramway" title="Leeds Tramway">electric tramway</a> led to intensification of development in Headingley and Potternewton and expansion outside the borough into Roundhay.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Two private gas supply companies were taken over by the corporation in 1870, and the municipal supply provided street lighting and cheaper gas to homes. From the early 1880s, the Yorkshire House-to-House Electricity Company supplied electricity to Leeds until it was purchased by Leeds Corporation and became a municipal supply.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Slum_clearance" title="Slum clearance">Slum clearance</a> and rebuilding began in Leeds during the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a> when over 18,000 houses were built by the council on 24 estates in <a href="/wiki/Cross_Gates" title="Cross Gates">Cross Gates</a>, Middleton, Gipton, Belle Isle and Halton Moor. The slums of <a href="/wiki/Quarry_Hill,_Leeds" title="Quarry Hill, Leeds">Quarry Hill</a> were replaced by the innovative Quarry Hill flats, which were demolished in 1975. Another 36,000 houses were built by private sector builders, creating suburbs in Gledhow, Moortown, Alwoodley, Roundhay, Colton, Whitkirk, <a href="/wiki/Oakwood,_Leeds" title="Oakwood, Leeds">Oakwood</a>, Weetwood, and Adel. After 1949 a further 30,000 sub-standard houses were demolished by the council and replaced by 151 medium-rise and high-rise blocks of council flats in estates at Seacroft, Armley Heights, Tinshill, and Brackenwood.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds has seen great expenditure on regenerating the city, attracting in investments and flagship projects,<sup id="cite_ref-leeds_skyscraper_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeds_skyscraper-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> as found in <a href="/wiki/Leeds_city_centre" title="Leeds city centre">Leeds city centre</a>. Many developments boasting luxurious penthouse apartments have been built close to the city centre.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_in_West_Yorkshire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="This map shows the locations of Leeds (coloured pink) and the other four metropolitan boroughs of West Yorkshire (clockwise from Leeds: Wakefield, Kirklees, Calderdale and Bradford). County and borough boundaries are black, urban areas grey, motorways blue with white stripe, rivers and bodies of water light blue. An inset shows a map of Great Britain with the location of West Yorkshire highlighted." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Leeds_in_West_Yorkshire.jpg/220px-Leeds_in_West_Yorkshire.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Leeds_in_West_Yorkshire.jpg/330px-Leeds_in_West_Yorkshire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Leeds_in_West_Yorkshire.jpg/440px-Leeds_in_West_Yorkshire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="558" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_in_West_Yorkshire.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Leeds in West Yorkshire</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:River_Aire_waterfront,_Leeds_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The canalised River Aire flows from the Dark Arches under Leeds&#39;s main railway station towards the bottom of the picture. To the left of the river is the lock which links the river with the Leeds and Liverpool Canal. To the right is a riverside walk beneath modern buildings, and in the distance, beyond the railway viaduct and station, are more high-rise modern buildings located on the west side of the city centre." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/River_Aire_waterfront%2C_Leeds_001.jpg/220px-River_Aire_waterfront%2C_Leeds_001.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/River_Aire_waterfront%2C_Leeds_001.jpg/330px-River_Aire_waterfront%2C_Leeds_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/River_Aire_waterfront%2C_Leeds_001.jpg/440px-River_Aire_waterfront%2C_Leeds_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2432" data-file-height="1793" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:River_Aire_waterfront,_Leeds_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>River Aire in Leeds</div></div></div>\n<p>Leeds is located 190 miles (310&#160;km) north-northwest of <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">London</a>, on the valley of the <a href="/wiki/River_Aire" title="River Aire">River Aire</a> in the eastern foothills of the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a>. The city centre lies in a narrow section of the Aire Valley at about 206 feet (63&#160;m) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a>; while the district ranges from 1,115 feet (340&#160;m) in the far west on the slopes of <a href="/wiki/Ilkley_Moor" title="Ilkley Moor">Ilkley Moor</a> to about 33 feet (10&#160;m) where the rivers Aire and Wharfe cross the eastern boundary. The centre of Leeds is part of a continuously built-up area extending to Pudsey, Bramley, Horsforth, Alwoodley, Seacroft, Middleton and Morley.<sup id="cite_ref-UAmap_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UAmap-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_population" title="List of English districts by population">second-highest population</a> of any local authority district in the UK (after <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_area" title="List of English districts by area">second-greatest area</a> of any English <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_borough" title="Metropolitan borough">metropolitan district</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Doncaster" title="Metropolitan Borough of Doncaster">Doncaster</a>), extending 15 miles (24&#160;km) from east to west, and 13 miles (21&#160;km) from north to south. The northern boundary follows the <a href="/wiki/River_Wharfe" title="River Wharfe">River Wharfe</a> for several miles, but it crosses the river to include the part of Otley which lies north of the river.\n</p><p>The city centre is less than twenty miles (32&#160;km) from the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Dales" title="Yorkshire Dales">Yorkshire Dales National Park</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> which has some of the most spectacular scenery and countryside in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Inner and southern areas of Leeds lie on a layer of coal measure sandstones forming the <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire_Coalfield" title="South Yorkshire Coalfield">Yorkshire Coalfield</a>. To the north parts are built on older sandstone and gritstones and to the east it extends into the magnesian limestone belt.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraser_1982_144_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraser_1982_144-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kendall_&amp;_Wroot_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kendall_&amp;_Wroot-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Land_use" title="Land use">land use</a> in the central areas of Leeds is overwhelmingly urban.<sup id="cite_ref-UAmap_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UAmap-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Attempts to define the exact geographic meaning of Leeds lead to a variety of concepts of its extent, varying by context include the area of the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_city_centre" title="Leeds city centre">city centre</a>, the urban sprawl, the administrative boundaries, and the functional <a href="/wiki/Region" title="Region">region</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraser_1982_456_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraser_1982_456-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Leeds is much more a generalised concept place name in inverted commas, it is the city, but it is also the commuter villages and the region as well.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>Brian Thompson, A History of Modern Leeds<sup id="cite_ref-Fraser_1982_456_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraser_1982_456-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_city_centre" title="Leeds city centre">Leeds city centre</a> is contained within the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Inner_Ring_Road" title="Leeds Inner Ring Road">Leeds Inner Ring Road</a>, formed from parts of the <a href="/wiki/A58_road" title="A58 road">A58 road</a>, <a href="/wiki/A61_road" title="A61 road">A61 road</a>, <a href="/wiki/A64_road" title="A64 road">A64 road</a>, <a href="/wiki/A643_road" title="A643 road">A643 road</a> and the <a href="/wiki/M621_motorway" title="M621 motorway">M621 motorway</a>. <a href="/wiki/Briggate,_Leeds" title="Briggate, Leeds">Briggate</a>, the principal north-south shopping street, is pedestrianised and Queen Victoria Street, a part of the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Quarter" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Quarter">Victoria Quarter</a>, is enclosed under a glass roof. <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Square_(Leeds)" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Square (Leeds)">Millennium Square</a> is a significant urban focal point. The <a href="/wiki/LS_postcode_area" title="LS postcode area">Leeds postcode area</a> covers most of the City of Leeds<sup id="cite_ref-postal_council_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-postal_council-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and is almost entirely made up of the Leeds <a href="/wiki/Post_town" title="Post town">post town</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mail_guide_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mail_guide-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Otley, Wetherby, Tadcaster, Pudsey and Ilkley are separate post towns within the postcode area.<sup id="cite_ref-mail_guide_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mail_guide-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Aside from the built up area of Leeds itself, there are a <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_Leeds" title="List of places in Leeds">number of suburbs and exurbs</a> within the district.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Park_Square_and_Leeds_Town_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_183544.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Park_Square_and_Leeds_Town_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_183544.jpg/220px-Park_Square_and_Leeds_Town_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_183544.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Park_Square_and_Leeds_Town_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_183544.jpg/330px-Park_Square_and_Leeds_Town_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_183544.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Park_Square_and_Leeds_Town_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_183544.jpg/440px-Park_Square_and_Leeds_Town_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_183544.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Park_Square_and_Leeds_Town_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_183544.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sunny early-June 2006 day at <a href="/wiki/Park_Square,_Leeds" title="Park Square, Leeds">Park Square</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Leeds has a climate that is <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic</a>, and influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a>. Summers are usually mild, with moderate rainfall, while winters are chilly, cloudy with occasional snow and frost. The nearest official weather recording station is at Bingley, some twenty kilometres away at a higher altitude.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Situated on the eastern side of the Pennines, Leeds is among the drier cities in the United Kingdom, with an annual rainfall of 660&#160;mm (25.98&#160;in).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The last reported tornado occurred on 14 September 2006, causing uprooted trees and signal failures at <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds City railway station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_belt">Green belt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Green belt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/South_and_West_Yorkshire_Green_Belt" title="South and West Yorkshire Green Belt">South and West Yorkshire Green Belt</a></div>\n<p>Leeds is within a <a href="/wiki/Green_belt_(United_Kingdom)" title="Green belt (United Kingdom)">green belt</a> region that extends into the wider surrounding counties, and is in place to reduce <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>, prevent the settlements in the West Yorkshire conurbation from further convergence, protect the identity of outlying communities, encourage <a href="/wiki/Brownfield_land" title="Brownfield land">brownfield</a> reuse, and preserve nearby countryside. This is achieved by restricting inappropriate development within the designated areas, and imposing stricter conditions on permitted building.<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Over 60% of the Leeds district is green belt land and it surrounds the settlement, preventing further sprawl towards nearby communities. Larger outlying towns and villages are exempt from the green belt area. However, smaller villages, hamlets and rural areas are \'washed over\' by the designation. The green belt was first adopted in 1960,<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and the size in the borough in 2017 amounted to some 33,970 hectares (339.7&#160;km<sup>2</sup>; 131.2&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A subsidiary aim of the green belt is to encourage recreation and leisure interests,<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> with rural landscape features, greenfield areas and facilities including Temple Newsam Park and House with golf course, Rothwell Country Park, Middleton Park, Kirkstall Abbey ruins and surrounding park, Bedquilts recreation grounds, Waterloo lake, Roundhay castle and park, and Morwick, Cobble and Elmete Halls.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Leeds" title="Demography of Leeds">Demography of Leeds</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_subdivision">Urban subdivision</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Urban subdivision">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small><i>(April 2016)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>At the time of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">United Kingdom Census 2001</a>, the Leeds urban subdivision occupied an area of 109 square kilometres (42&#160;sq&#160;mi) and had a population of&#160;443,247; making it the fourth-most populous urban subdivision within England and the fifth largest within the United Kingdom. The population density was 4,066 inhabitants per square kilometre (10,530/sq&#160;mi), slightly higher than the rest of the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Urban_Area" title="West Yorkshire Urban Area">West Yorkshire Urban Area</a>. It accounts for 20% of the area and 62% of the population of the City of Leeds. The population of the urban subdivision had a 100&#160;to&#160;93.1&#160;female\xe2\x80\x93male ratio.<sup id="cite_ref-urban_pop_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urban_pop-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Of those over 16&#160;years old, 39.4% were single (never married) and 35.4% married for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-marital_pop_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marital_pop-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The urban subdivision\'s 188,890&#160;households included 35% one-person, 27.9% married couples living together, 8.8% were co-habiting couples, and 5.7% single parents with their children. Leeds is the largest component of the West Yorkshire Urban Area<sup id="cite_ref-UAmap_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UAmap-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and is counted by <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> as part of the Leeds-Bradford <a href="/wiki/Larger_urban_zone" title="Larger urban zone">larger urban zone</a>. The Leeds <a href="/wiki/Travel_to_work_area" title="Travel to work area">travel to work area</a> in 2001 included all of the City of Leeds, a northern strip of the City of Bradford, the eastern part of Kirklees, and a section of southern North Yorkshire; it occupies 751 square kilometres (290&#160;sq&#160;mi).\n</p><p>In 2011, the Leeds USD had a population of 474,632 and had an area of 112 square kilometres (70 square miles) with a population density of 4,238 people per square kilometre and 6,780 per square mile.<sup id="cite_ref-citypopulation.de_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citypopulation.de-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> It is bounded by, and physically attached to, the other towns of <a href="/wiki/Garforth" title="Garforth">Garforth</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Morley,_West_Yorkshire" title="Morley, West Yorkshire">Morley</a> to the southwest and <a href="/wiki/Pudsey" title="Pudsey">Pudsey</a> to the west, all being within the wider borough. 63% of the borough\'s population of 751,485 live in the USD, while it takes up only 21% of its area.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Leeds compared</th>\n<th>Leeds USD</th>\n<th>Leeds City\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>White British</td>\n<td>73.9%</td>\n<td>81.1%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Asian</td>\n<td>10.7%</td>\n<td>7.7%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Black</td>\n<td>5.2%</td>\n<td>3.5%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, the Leeds USD (Urban Subdivision) had a total \'White\' population of 79.1%<sup id="cite_ref-citypopulation.de_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citypopulation.de-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> with this percentage including people from places such as mainland Europe and Ireland. This makes the USD about as multicultural as <a href="/wiki/Salford,_Greater_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Salford, Greater Manchester">Salford</a> in Greater Manchester. The USD is what is commonly regarded as being Leeds itself, however it is the wider borough that has been given city status.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_district">Metropolitan district</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Metropolitan district">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At the time of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 UK Census</a>, the district had a total population of 751,500, representing a 5% growth since the previous census ten years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-westyorkshireobservatory.org_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-westyorkshireobservatory.org-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> According to the 2001 UK Census, there were 301,614 households in Leeds; 33.3% were married couples living together, 31.6% were single-person households, 9.0% were <a href="/wiki/Cohabitation" title="Cohabitation">co-habiting</a> couples and 9.8% were single parents, following a similar trend to the rest of England.<sup id="cite_ref-household_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-household-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The population density was 1,967/km<sup>2</sup> (5,090/sq&#160;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-household_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-household-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> and for every 100 females, there were 93.5 males.\n</p><p>Leeds is a diverse city with over 75 ethnic groups, and with ethnic minorities representing just under 11.6% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-westyorkshireobservatory.org_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-westyorkshireobservatory.org-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> According to figures from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 UK Census</a>, 85.0% of the population was <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a> (81.1% <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White British</a>, 0.9% <a href="/wiki/Irish_migration_to_Great_Britain" title="Irish migration to Great Britain">White Irish</a>, 0.1% <a href="/wiki/Gypsy_(term)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gypsy (term)">Gypsy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Irish_Traveller" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Traveller">Irish Traveller</a>, 2.9% <a href="/wiki/Other_White" title="Other White">Other White</a>), 2.7% of <a href="/wiki/Mixed_(United_Kingdom_ethnicity_category)" title="Mixed (United Kingdom ethnicity category)">mixed race</a> (1.2% White and Black Caribbean, 0.3% White and Black African, 0.7% White and Asian, 0.5% Other Mixed), 7.7% <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">Asian</a> (2.1% <a href="/wiki/British_Indian" title="British Indian">Indian</a>, 3.0% <a href="/wiki/British_Pakistanis" title="British Pakistanis">Pakistani</a>, 0.6% <a href="/wiki/British_Bangladeshi" title="British Bangladeshi">Bangladeshi</a>, 0.8% <a href="/wiki/British_Chinese" title="British Chinese">Chinese</a>, 1.2% Other Asian), 3.5% <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Black</a> (2.0% African, 0.9% <a href="/wiki/British_African-Caribbean_people" title="British African-Caribbean people">Caribbean</a>, 0.6% <a href="/wiki/Other_Black" class="mw-redirect" title="Other Black">Other Black</a>), 0.5% <a href="/wiki/British_Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="British Arab">Arab</a> and 0.6% of other ethnic heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The majority of people in Leeds identify themselves as Christian.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_Data_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_Data-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The proportion of Muslims (3.0% of the population) is average for the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_Data_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_Data-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Leeds has the third-largest community of Jews in the United Kingdom, after those of London and Manchester. The areas of <a href="/wiki/Alwoodley" title="Alwoodley">Alwoodley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moortown,_Leeds" title="Moortown, Leeds">Moortown</a> contain sizeable Jewish communities.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedman_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedman-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> 16.8% of Leeds residents in the 2001 census declared themselves as having "No Religion", which is broadly in line with the figure for the whole of the UK (also 8.1% "religion not stated"). The crime rate in Leeds is well above the national average, like many other English major cities.<sup id="cite_ref-crime_street_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crime_street-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-crime_stat_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crime_stat-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In July 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tank</a> <a href="/wiki/Reform_(think_tank)" title="Reform (think tank)">Reform</a> calculated rates of crime for different offences and has related this to populations of major urban areas (defined as towns over 100,000 population). Leeds was 11th in this rating (excluding London boroughs, 23rd including London boroughs).<sup id="cite_ref-reform_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reform-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Total recorded crime in Leeds fell by 45% between 2002/03 and 2011/12.<sup id="cite_ref-westyorkshireobservatory.org_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-westyorkshireobservatory.org-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The table below details the population of the current area of the district since 1801, including the percentage change since the last available census data.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:40%; width:40%; border:0; text-align:center; line-height:120%;">\n<caption><a href="/wiki/Population_growth" href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/City_of_Leeds" title="City of Leeds">City of Leeds</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Civic_Hall_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Civic_Hall_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg/220px-Civic_Hall_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Civic_Hall_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg/330px-Civic_Hall_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Civic_Hall_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg/440px-Civic_Hall_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1583" data-file-height="1583" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Civic_Hall_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Civic_Hall" title="Leeds Civic Hall">Leeds Civic Hall</a> is the seat of local government.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/City_of_Leeds" title="City of Leeds">City of Leeds</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_England" title="Districts of England">local government district</a> covering Leeds, and the local authority is <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Council" title="Leeds City Council">Leeds City Council</a>. The council is composed of 99 councillors, three for each of the district\'s <a href="/wiki/Wards_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Wards of the United Kingdom">wards</a>. Elections are held three years out of four, on the first Thursday of May. One third of the councillors are elected, for a four-year term, in each election. The council is currently controlled by <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>. <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a> does not have a county council, so Leeds City Council is the primary provider of local government services for the city. The district is in the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">Yorkshire and the Humber</a> region of England.\n</p><p>Most of the district is an <a href="/wiki/Unparished_area" title="Unparished area">unparished area</a>. In the unparished area, there is no lower tier of government. Outside the unparished area, there are 31 <a href="/wiki/Civil_parish" title="Civil parish">civil parishes</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Parish_councils_in_England" title="Parish councils in England">parish councils</a>. These are the lowest tier of local government<sup id="cite_ref-leeds_parish_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeds_parish-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> and absorb some limited functions from Leeds City Council in their areas.\n</p><p>The district is represented by eight <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MPs</a>, for the constituencies of <a href="/wiki/Elmet_and_Rothwell_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Elmet and Rothwell (UK Parliament constituency)">Elmet and Rothwell</a> (<a href="/wiki/Alec_Shelbrooke" title="Alec Shelbrooke">Alec Shelbrooke</a>, Conservative); <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Central_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Leeds Central (UK Parliament constituency)">Leeds Central</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hilary_Benn" title="Hilary Benn">Hilary Benn</a>, Labour); <a href="/wiki/Leeds_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Leeds East (UK Parliament constituency)">Leeds East</a> (<a href="/wiki/Richard_Burgon" title="Richard Burgon">Richard Burgon</a>, Labour); <a href="/wiki/Leeds_North_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Leeds North East (UK Parliament constituency)">Leeds North East</a> (<a href="/wiki/Fabian_Hamilton" title="Fabian Hamilton">Fabian Hamilton</a>, Labour); <a href="/wiki/Leeds_North_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Leeds North West (UK Parliament constituency)">Leeds North West</a> (<a href="/wiki/Alex_Sobel" title="Alex Sobel">Alex Sobel</a>, Labour); <a href="/wiki/Leeds_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Leeds West (UK Parliament constituency)">Leeds West</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rachel_Reeves" title="Rachel Reeves">Rachel Reeves</a>, Labour); <a href="/wiki/Morley_and_Outwood_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Morley and Outwood (UK Parliament constituency)">Morley and Outwood</a> (constituency shared with <a href="/wiki/City_of_Wakefield" title="City of Wakefield">City of Wakefield</a>) (<a href="/wiki/Andrea_Jenkyns" title="Andrea Jenkyns">Andrea Jenkyns</a>, Conservative); and <a href="/wiki/Pudsey_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Pudsey (UK Parliament constituency)">Pudsey</a> (<a href="/wiki/Stuart_Andrew" title="Stuart Andrew">Stuart Andrew</a>, Conservative). Leeds is within the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Yorkshire and the Humber (European Parliament constituency)">Yorkshire and the Humber</a> European constituency, which as of  May 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> is represented by two <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Independence_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Independence Party">UKIP</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>, and two <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Members of the European Parliament</a>.\n</p><p>In addition to other national governmental offices, the city is home to a large <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Work_and_Pensions" title="Department for Work and Pensions">Department for Work and Pensions</a> office building located in <a href="/wiki/Quarry_Hill,_Leeds" title="Quarry Hill, Leeds">Quarry Hill</a>, notable for its imposing design.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Leeds" title="Economy of Leeds">Economy of Leeds</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Infirmary_Street,_Leeds_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Infirmary_Street%2C_Leeds_2012.jpg/220px-Infirmary_Street%2C_Leeds_2012.jpg" width="220" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Infirmary_Street%2C_Leeds_2012.jpg/330px-Infirmary_Street%2C_Leeds_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Infirmary_Street%2C_Leeds_2012.jpg/440px-Infirmary_Street%2C_Leeds_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="3562" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Infirmary_Street,_Leeds_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Infirmary Street in the heart of Leeds\' Financial District</div></div></div>\n<p>Leeds has the most diverse economy of all the UK\'s main employment centres and has seen the fastest rate of private sector jobs growth of any UK city and has the highest ratio of public to private sector jobs of all the UK\'s Core Cities. The city has the third-largest jobs total by local authority area with 480,000 in employment and self-employment at the beginning of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> 24.7% were in public administration, education and health, 23.9% were in banking, finance and insurance and 21.4% were in distribution, hotels and restaurants. It is in the banking, finance and insurance sectors that Leeds differs most from the financial structure of the region and the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, the financial and services industry in Leeds was worth \xc2\xa32.1&#160;billion, the fifth-largest in the UK, behind London, Edinburgh, Manchester and Birmingham.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Tertiary industries such as retail, <a href="/wiki/Call_centre" title="Call centre">call centres</a>, offices and media have contributed to a high rate of economic growth. The city also hosts the only subsidiary office of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> in the UK. In 2012 GVA for the city was recorded at \xc2\xa318.8&#160;billion,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> with the entire <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Region" title="Leeds City Region">Leeds City Region</a> generating a \xc2\xa356&#160;billion economy.<sup id="cite_ref-leeds.gov.uk_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeds.gov.uk-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bridgewater_place,Leeds.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bridgewater_place%2CLeeds.JPG/220px-Bridgewater_place%2CLeeds.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bridgewater_place%2CLeeds.JPG/330px-Bridgewater_place%2CLeeds.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bridgewater_place%2CLeeds.JPG/440px-Bridgewater_place%2CLeeds.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bridgewater_place,Leeds.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bridgewater_Place" title="Bridgewater Place">Bridgewater Place</a></div></div></div>\n<p>It is the largest centre outside London for financial and business services. Over the next ten years, the economy is forecast to grow by 25% with financial and business services set to generate over half of GVA growth over that period with Finance and business services accounting for 38% of total output. Other key sectors include retail, leisure and the visitor economy, construction, manufacturing and the creative and digital industries.<sup id="cite_ref-leeds.gov.uk_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeds.gov.uk-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds has over 30 national and international banks, many of whose northern or regional offices are based in the city. It is the headquarters for <a href="/wiki/First_Direct" title="First Direct">First Direct</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Bank" title="Yorkshire Bank">Yorkshire Bank</a>, and has large <a href="/wiki/Barclays" title="Barclays">Barclays</a>, <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banco_Santander" title="Banco Santander">Santander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lloyds_Banking_Group" title="Lloyds Banking Group">Lloyds Banking Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Scotland_Group" title="Royal Bank of Scotland Group">RBS Group</a> operations.<sup id="cite_ref-locateinleeds.co.uk_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-locateinleeds.co.uk-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is also an important centre for equity, venture and risk finance. Founded in Leeds, the venture capital provider, YFM Equity Partners, is now the UK\'s largest provider of risk capital to small and medium-sized enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-locateinleeds.co.uk_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-locateinleeds.co.uk-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other major companies based in the city include <a href="/wiki/William_Hill_(bookmaker)" title="William Hill (bookmaker)">William Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Personal_Finance" title="International Personal Finance">International Personal Finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Building_Society" title="Leeds Building Society">Leeds Building Society</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Foods" title="Northern Foods">Northern Foods</a>. <a href="/wiki/Capita" title="Capita">Capita</a> Group, <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Direct_Line" title="Direct Line">Direct Line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aviva" title="Aviva">Aviva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Building_Society" title="Yorkshire Building Society">Yorkshire Building Society</a>, <a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica_Europe" title="Telef\xc3\xb3nica Europe">Telef\xc3\xb3nica Europe</a> (otherwise known as O2) and <a href="/wiki/TD_Waterhouse" title="TD Waterhouse">TD Waterhouse</a> all also have a considerable presence in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-locateinleeds.co.uk_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-locateinleeds.co.uk-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are around 150 law firms operating in Leeds, employing over 6,700 people. According to The UK Legal 500, "Leeds has a sophisticated and highly competitive legal market, second only to London."<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Specialist legal expertise to be found in Leeds includes corporate finance, corporate restructuring and insolvency, global project financing, trade and investment, commercial litigation, competition, construction, Private Finance Initiatives and Public Private Partnerships, tax, derivatives, IT, employment, pensions, intellectual property, sport and entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The establishment of an Administrative Court in Leeds in April 2009 reinforced Leeds\' position as one of the UK\'s key legal centres. The court previously sat only in London.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds is the UK\'s third-largest manufacturing centre and 50% of the UK\'s manufacturing base is within a two-hour drive of Leeds. With around 1,800 firms and 39,000 employees, Leeds manufacturing firms account for 8.8% of total employment in the city. The largest sub-sectors are engineering, printing and publishing, food and drink, chemicals and medical technology.<sup id="cite_ref-Leeds_2013_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leeds_2013-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is also an established creative industry in the city, particularly in the digital gaming sector. A number of large developers have studios in and around the city, including <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>, developers of the mobile versions of the <i><a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty" title="Call of Duty">Call of Duty</a></i> series, and <a href="/wiki/Rockstar_Leeds" title="Rockstar Leeds">Rockstar Leeds</a>, developers of the <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto" title="Grand Theft Auto">Grand Theft Auto</a></i> series.
