In 2009 Leeds was the first city outside London to host the <a href="/wiki/EGX_(expo)" title="EGX (expo)">Eurogamer Expo</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Park_Row_-_Leeds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Park_Row_-_Leeds.jpg/220px-Park_Row_-_Leeds.jpg" width="220" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Park_Row_-_Leeds.jpg/330px-Park_Row_-_Leeds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Park_Row_-_Leeds.jpg/440px-Park_Row_-_Leeds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Park_Row_-_Leeds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Park Row in Leeds\' Central Business District</div></div></div>\n<p>Office developments, also traditionally located in the inner area, have expanded south of the River Aire and total 11,000,000 square feet (1,000,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of space.<sup id="cite_ref-econ_leeds_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econ_leeds-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In the period from 1999 to 2008 \xc2\xa32.5bn of property development was undertaken in central Leeds; of which \xc2\xa3711m has been offices, \xc2\xa3265m retail, \xc2\xa3389m leisure and \xc2\xa3794m housing. Manufacturing and distribution uses accounts for \xc2\xa326m of new property development in the period. There are 130,100 jobs in the city centre, accounting for 31% of all jobs in the wider district. In 2007, 47,500 jobs were in finance and business, 42,300 in public services, and 19,500 in retail and distribution. 43% of finance sector jobs in the district are contained in Leeds city centre and 44% of those employed in the city centre live more than nine kilometres (5.6 miles) away.<sup id="cite_ref-econ_leeds_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econ_leeds-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tourism is important to the Leeds economy, in 2009 Leeds was the eighth-most visited city in England by UK visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> and the 13th-most visited city by overseas visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Research by <a href="/wiki/VisitEngland" title="VisitEngland">VisitEngland</a> reported that the day visitor market to Leeds attracts 24.9&#160;million people each year, worth over \xc2\xa3654&#160;million to the local economy.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Cond%C3%A9_Nast_Traveler" title="Cond\xc3\xa9 Nast Traveler">Cond\xc3\xa9 Nast Traveler</a> survey of readers, Leeds rated 6th among The 15 Best Cities in the UK for visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, Leeds received 27.29 million leisure tourist visits generating over \xc2\xa31.6bn for the city, according to data from a STEAM survey. That was a 15.9% increase in revenue over 2015. A 9.7% increase in visits had been recorded since 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The industry supported over 19,000 full-time equivalent jobs in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2011, Leeds was named as one of five "cities to watch" in a report published by <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Cities" title="Centre for Cities">Centre for Cities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The report shows that the average resident in Leeds earns \xc2\xa3471 per week,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> seventeenth nationally and 30.9% of Leeds residents had NVQ4+ high-level qualifications,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> fifteenth nationally. Employment in Leeds was 68.8% in the period June 2012 to June 2013, which was lower than the national average, whilst unemployment was higher than the national average at 9.6% over the same time period.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> It also shows that Leeds will be the least affected major city by welfare cuts in 2014/2015, with welfare cuts of \xc2\xa3125 per capita predicted, compared to \xc2\xa3192 in Liverpool and \xc2\xa3175 in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Leeds is overall less deprived than other large UK cities and average income is above regional averages.<sup id="cite_ref-westyorkshireobservatory.org_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-westyorkshireobservatory.org-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_sector">Public sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Public sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NHS_England_HQ.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/NHS_England_HQ.jpg/220px-NHS_England_HQ.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/NHS_England_HQ.jpg/330px-NHS_England_HQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/NHS_England_HQ.jpg/440px-NHS_England_HQ.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1582" data-file-height="890" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NHS_England_HQ.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/NHS_England" title="NHS England">NHS England</a> HQ.</div></div></div>\n<p>In Leeds, 108,000 people work in the public sector\xe2\x80\x9424% of the workforce. The largest employers are Leeds City Council, with 33,000 staff, and the Leeds Teaching Hospitals NHS Trust, with 14,000 staff.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds has become a hub of public-sector health bodies. The <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Health">Department of Health</a>, <a href="/wiki/NHS_England" title="NHS England">NHS England</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Care_Quality_Commission" title="Care Quality Commission">Care Quality Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/NHS_Digital" title="NHS Digital">NHS Digital</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Public_Health_England" title="Public Health England">Public Health England</a> all have large offices in Leeds. Europe\'s largest teaching hospital is also based in Leeds, and is home to the Yorkshire Cancer Centre, the largest of its kind in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Key government departments and organisations in Leeds include the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Work_and_Pensions" title="Department for Work and Pensions">Department for Work and Pensions</a>, with over 3,000 staff, the Department of Health, with over 800 staff, <a href="/wiki/HM_Revenue_and_Customs" title="HM Revenue and Customs">HM Revenue and Customs</a> with over 1,200 staff and the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a> with 1,100 staff.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:County_Arcade_Victoria_Quarter_Leeds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/County_Arcade_Victoria_Quarter_Leeds.jpg/220px-County_Arcade_Victoria_Quarter_Leeds.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/County_Arcade_Victoria_Quarter_Leeds.jpg/330px-County_Arcade_Victoria_Quarter_Leeds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/County_Arcade_Victoria_Quarter_Leeds.jpg/440px-County_Arcade_Victoria_Quarter_Leeds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:County_Arcade_Victoria_Quarter_Leeds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Victoria_Quarter" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Quarter">Victoria Quarter</a>.  <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:King-edward-street-leeds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/King-edward-street-leeds.jpg/220px-King-edward-street-leeds.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/King-edward-street-leeds.jpg/330px-King-edward-street-leeds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/King-edward-street-leeds.jpg/440px-King-edward-street-leeds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:King-edward-street-leeds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>King Edward Street</div></div></div> Opened in 1900</div></div></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pinnacle,_Leeds_16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Pinnacle%2C_Leeds_16.jpg/220px-Pinnacle%2C_Leeds_16.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Pinnacle%2C_Leeds_16.jpg/330px-Pinnacle%2C_Leeds_16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Pinnacle%2C_Leeds_16.jpg/440px-Pinnacle%2C_Leeds_16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pinnacle,_Leeds_16.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Trinity_Leeds" title="Trinity Leeds">Trinity Leeds</a> is Leeds\' largest shopping centre</div></div></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Opening_day,_Victoria_Gate,_Leeds_(20th_October_2016)_004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Opening_day%2C_Victoria_Gate%2C_Leeds_%2820th_October_2016%29_004.jpg/220px-Opening_day%2C_Victoria_Gate%2C_Leeds_%2820th_October_2016%29_004.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Opening_day%2C_Victoria_Gate%2C_Leeds_%2820th_October_2016%29_004.jpg/330px-Opening_day%2C_Victoria_Gate%2C_Leeds_%2820th_October_2016%29_004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Opening_day%2C_Victoria_Gate%2C_Leeds_%2820th_October_2016%29_004.jpg/440px-Opening_day%2C_Victoria_Gate%2C_Leeds_%2820th_October_2016%29_004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5152" data-file-height="3864" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Opening_day,_Victoria_Gate,_Leeds_(20th_October_2016)_004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Victoria_Gate" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Gate">Victoria Gate</a> is Leeds\' newest shopping centre</div></div></div>\n<p>The extensive retail area of Leeds is identified as the principal regional shopping centre for the whole of the Yorkshire and the Humber region with a catchment of 5.5&#160;million people offering a spend of \xc2\xa31.93&#160;billion annually.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> There are a number of indoor shopping centres in the centre of the city, including the <a href="/wiki/Merrion_Centre,_Leeds" title="Merrion Centre, Leeds">Merrion Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_John%27s_Centre" title="St John&#39;s Centre">St John\'s Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schofields_(department_store)" title="Schofields (department store)">The Core</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Quarter" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Quarter">Victoria Quarter</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Light_(Leeds)" title="The Light (Leeds)">The Light</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Corn_Exchange" title="Leeds Corn Exchange">Corn Exchange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Leeds" title="Trinity Leeds">Trinity Leeds</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Gate" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Gate">Victoria Gate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In total there are well over 1,000 retail stores, with a combined floorspace of 3,660,000 square feet (340,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-econ_leeds_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econ_leeds-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> in Leeds City Centre.\n</p><p>The city centre has a large <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian_zone" title="Pedestrian zone">pedestrian zone</a>. <a href="/wiki/Briggate" class="mw-redirect" title="Briggate">Briggate</a> is the main shopping street where one can find many well-known British <a href="/wiki/High_Street" title="High Street">High Street</a> stores, including <a href="/wiki/Marks_%26_Spencer" title="Marks &amp; Spencer">Marks &amp; Spencer</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_of_Fraser" title="House of Fraser">House of Fraser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Debenhams" title="Debenhams">Debenhams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Topshop" title="Topshop">Topshop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costa_Coffee" title="Costa Coffee">Costa Coffee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Nichols" title="Harvey Nichols">Harvey Nichols</a>. Many companies have several stores within Central Leeds and the wider city. The <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Quarter" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Quarter">Victoria Quarter</a> is notable for its high-end luxury retailers and impressive architecture. 70 stores such as <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vivienne_Westwood" title="Vivienne Westwood">Vivienne Westwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Smith_(fashion_designer)" title="Paul Smith (fashion designer)">Paul Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diesel_(brand)" title="Diesel (brand)">Diesel</a> and anchor <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Nichols" title="Harvey Nichols">Harvey Nichols</a> are contained within two iron-wrought Victorian arcades, and a new arcade formed by arcading Queen Victoria Street with the largest expanse of stained glass in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the Churwell area of Leeds is the <a href="/wiki/White_Rose_Shopping_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="White Rose Shopping Centre">White Rose Shopping Centre</a>. Opening in 1997, the centre has over 100 high street stores anchored by Debenhams, Marks &amp; Spencer, Primark and Sainsbury\'s. Some stores have their only Leeds presence here and do not trade in Central Leeds, such as the Disney Store and Build-A-Bear workshop. Although the centre is below the average typical size for out of town shopping malls like the <a href="/wiki/Trafford_Centre" title="Trafford Centre">Trafford Centre</a> or <a href="/wiki/Meadowhall_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Meadowhall Centre">Meadowhall</a> in nearby Yorkshire city <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, it remains popular with national and international chains. Of the 40,000 people who work in retailing in Leeds 75% work in places which are not located in the city centre. There are additional shopping centres located in the many villages that became part of the county borough and in the towns that were incorporated in the City of Leeds in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 March 2013, a large shopping and leisure complex called <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Leeds" title="Trinity Leeds">Trinity Leeds</a> opened in the city centre. The modern and interactive retail space covers the old Burton Arcades and the former <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Leeds" title="Trinity Leeds">Leeds Shopping Plaza</a> with its main entrance from Briggate.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 October 2016, the newest shopping destination called <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Gate" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Gate">Victoria Gate</a> opened its doors to the public. The new shopping mall houses a flagship <a href="/wiki/John_Lewis_(department_store)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Lewis (department store)">John Lewis</a> store, the largest outside London. Seventy-five per cent of the stores that opened in Victoria Gate were new to Leeds with many of those stores being the first outside of London.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:General_Post_Office,_City_Square,_Leeds_(former)_(4824877432).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/General_Post_Office%2C_City_Square%2C_Leeds_%28former%29_%284824877432%29.jpg/220px-General_Post_Office%2C_City_Square%2C_Leeds_%28former%29_%284824877432%29.jpg" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/General_Post_Office%2C_City_Square%2C_Leeds_%28former%29_%284824877432%29.jpg/330px-General_Post_Office%2C_City_Square%2C_Leeds_%28former%29_%284824877432%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/General_Post_Office%2C_City_Square%2C_Leeds_%28former%29_%284824877432%29.jpg/440px-General_Post_Office%2C_City_Square%2C_Leeds_%28former%29_%284824877432%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2260" data-file-height="1840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:General_Post_Office,_City_Square,_Leeds_(former)_(4824877432).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Square" title="Leeds City Square">The Old Post Office in Leeds City Square</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirkstall_Abbey_at_sunset.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Kirkstall_Abbey_at_sunset.jpg/220px-Kirkstall_Abbey_at_sunset.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Kirkstall_Abbey_at_sunset.jpg/330px-Kirkstall_Abbey_at_sunset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Kirkstall_Abbey_at_sunset.jpg/440px-Kirkstall_Abbey_at_sunset.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4886" data-file-height="3062" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirkstall_Abbey_at_sunset.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kirkstall_Abbey" title="Kirkstall Abbey">Kirkstall Abbey</a>. Founded c.1152</div></div></div>\n<p>Leeds displays a variety of natural and built landmarks. Natural landmarks include such diverse sites as the gritstone outcrop of <a href="/wiki/The_Chevin" title="The Chevin">Otley Chevin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fairburn_Ings_RSPB_reserve" title="Fairburn Ings RSPB reserve">Fairburn Ings RSPB reserve</a>. The city\'s parks at <a href="/wiki/Roundhay_Park" title="Roundhay Park">Roundhay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Temple_Newsam" title="Temple Newsam">Temple Newsam</a> have long been owned and maintained by the council for the benefit of ratepayers and among the open spaces in the centre of Leeds are <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Square,_Leeds" title="Millennium Square, Leeds">Millennium Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Square" title="Leeds City Square">City Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Park_Square,_Leeds" title="Park Square, Leeds">Park Square</a> and Victoria Gardens. This last is the site of the central city <a href="/wiki/War_memorial" title="War memorial">war memorial</a>: there are 42 other war memorials in the suburbs, towns and villages in the district.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The built environment embraces edifices of civic pride like <a href="/wiki/Morley_Town_Hall" title="Morley Town Hall">Morley Town Hall</a> and the trio of buildings in Leeds, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Town_Hall" title="Leeds Town Hall">Leeds Town Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Corn_Exchange" title="Leeds Corn Exchange">Corn Exchange</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Museum" title="Leeds City Museum">Leeds City Museum</a> by the architect <a href="/wiki/Cuthbert_Brodrick" title="Cuthbert Brodrick">Cuthbert Brodrick</a>. The two white buildings on the Leeds skyline are the Parkinson building of Leeds University and the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Civic_Hall" title="Leeds Civic Hall">Civic Hall</a>, with golden owls adorning the tops of the latter\'s twin spires.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Armley_Mills" class="mw-redirect" title="Armley Mills">Armley Mills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tower_Works" title="Tower Works">Tower Works</a>, with its campanile-inspired towers, and the Egyptian-style <a href="/wiki/Temple_Works" title="Temple Works">Temple Works</a> hark back to the city\'s industrial past, while the site and ruins of <a href="/wiki/Kirkstall_Abbey" title="Kirkstall Abbey">Kirkstall Abbey</a> display the beauty and grandeur of <a href="/wiki/Cistercian" class="mw-redirect" title="Cistercian">Cistercian</a> architecture. Notable churches are <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Minster" title="Leeds Minster">Leeds Minster</a> (formerly Leeds Parish Church), <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Church,_Leeds" title="St George&#39;s Church, Leeds">St George\'s Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Cathedral" title="Leeds Cathedral">Leeds Cathedral</a>, in the city centre, and the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St_John_the_Baptist,_Adel" class="mw-redirect" title="Church of St John the Baptist, Adel">Church of St John the Baptist, Adel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bardsey,_West_Yorkshire" title="Bardsey, West Yorkshire">Bardsey</a> Parish Church in quieter locations. Notable <a href="/wiki/Non-conformist" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-conformist">non-conformist</a> chapels include the <a href="/wiki/Salem_Chapel,_Leeds" title="Salem Chapel, Leeds">Salem Chapel</a>, dating back to 1791 and notably the birthplace of Leeds United Football Club in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds is one of only a few UK cities outside of London to have a significant number of <a href="/wiki/High-rise_building" title="High-rise building">high-rise buildings</a>, the 112-metre (367&#160;ft) tower of <a href="/wiki/Bridgewater_Place" title="Bridgewater Place">Bridgewater Place</a>, also known as <i>The Dalek</i>, is part of a major office and residential development and the region\'s tallest building; it can be seen for miles around.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Bridgewater Place has been the subject of debate as its erection in 2007 caused significant <a href="/wiki/Wind_tunnel" title="Wind tunnel">wind tunnel</a> effects, channeling strong wind currents across Victoria Road. There have been numerous injuries attributed to the inadequate architecture of this building<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> and Water Lane is frequently closed when high winds are expected. <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Council" title="Leeds City Council">Leeds City Council</a> are undertaking construction work in an attempt to deflect the wind from street level and the building owners of Bridgewater Place agreed to pay to cover the public money being spent.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Among other Skyscrapers the 37-storey <a href="/wiki/Sky_Plaza" title="Sky Plaza">Sky Plaza</a> to the north of the city centre stands on higher ground so that its 106 metres (348&#160;ft) is higher than Bridgewater Place.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a> (football) and <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Stadium" title="Headingley Stadium">Headingley Stadium</a> (cricket and rugby) are well known to sports enthusiasts and the <a href="/wiki/White_Rose_Centre" title="White Rose Centre">White Rose Centre</a> is a well-known retail outlet. Headingley Carnegie Stadium is also home to Leeds Rhinos rugby team.\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leedsskylineatnight.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Leedsskylineatnight.jpg/750px-Leedsskylineatnight.jpg" width="750" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Leedsskylineatnight.jpg/1125px-Leedsskylineatnight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Leedsskylineatnight.jpg/1500px-Leedsskylineatnight.jpg 2x" data-file-width="15483" data-file-height="2399" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leedsskylineatnight.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leeds city centre, viewed from South Leeds at night</div></div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Leeds" title="Transport in Leeds">Transport in Leeds</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moor_Road_Underpass_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1600451.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Moor_Road_Underpass_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1600451.jpg/220px-Moor_Road_Underpass_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1600451.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Moor_Road_Underpass_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1600451.jpg/330px-Moor_Road_Underpass_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1600451.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Moor_Road_Underpass_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1600451.jpg/440px-Moor_Road_Underpass_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1600451.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moor_Road_Underpass_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1600451.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>M621 heading towards Central Leeds</div></div></div>\n<p>Leeds is the starting point of the <a href="/wiki/A62_road" title="A62 road">A62</a>, <a href="/wiki/A63_road" title="A63 road">A63</a>, <a href="/wiki/A64_road" title="A64 road">A64</a>, <a href="/wiki/A65_road" title="A65 road">A65</a> and <a href="/wiki/A660_road" title="A660 road">A660</a> roads, and is also situated on the <a href="/wiki/A58_road" title="A58 road">A58</a> and <a href="/wiki/A61_road" title="A61 road">A61</a>. The <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1</a> and <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62</a> intersect to its south and the <a href="/wiki/A1(M)_motorway" title="A1(M) motorway">A1(M)</a> passes to the east. Leeds is one of the principal hubs of the northern motorway network. Additionally, there is an urban motorway network; the radial <a href="/wiki/M621_motorway" title="M621 motorway">M621</a> takes traffic into central Leeds from the M62 and M1. There is an <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Inner_Ring_Road" title="Leeds Inner Ring Road">Inner Ring Road</a> with part motorway status and an <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Outer_Ring_Road" title="Leeds Outer Ring Road">Outer Ring Road</a>. Part of the city centre<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> is pedestrianised, and is encircled by the clockwise-only <a href="/wiki/List_of_junctions_on_Leeds_City_Centre_Loop_Road" title="List of junctions on Leeds City Centre Loop Road">Loop Road</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_city_railway_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Leeds_city_railway_station.jpg/220px-Leeds_city_railway_station.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Leeds_city_railway_station.jpg/330px-Leeds_city_railway_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Leeds_city_railway_station.jpg/440px-Leeds_city_railway_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_city_railway_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds railway station</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LBIA_terminal_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/LBIA_terminal_1.jpg/220px-LBIA_terminal_1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/LBIA_terminal_1.jpg/330px-LBIA_terminal_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/LBIA_terminal_1.jpg/440px-LBIA_terminal_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LBIA_terminal_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bradford_Airport" title="Leeds Bradford Airport">Leeds Bradford International Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Leeds has been identified as one of the most car-dependent cities in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In one 2012 study of 31 European cities, Leeds-Bradford was rated as the seventh-most grid-locked.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Drivers spend an average of 80 hours in congestion.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Measurements taken on some main roads in Leeds have revealed pollution levels over twice the legal limits.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The main reason for these problems is the fact that unlike other cities in the UK similar in size to Leeds, such as <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, Leeds does not have a rapid transport system (such as the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Manchester Metrolink</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Sheffield Supertram</a>). Therefore, commuters tend to either drive or use buses, which can be delayed when the roads are congested. There were plans for a <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Supertram" title="Leeds Supertram">Leeds Supertram</a> in the 1990s, and \xc2\xa3500&#160;million in funding was to be provided; however, due to spiraling costs the plans were cancelled by the Transport Minister <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Darling" title="Alistair Darling">Alistair Darling</a> in 2005, even though \xc2\xa340&#160;million had already been spent on the project. Hopes were renewed with the proposal for a \xc2\xa3250&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Leeds" title="Trolleybuses in Leeds">New Generation Transport</a> Trolleybus service in 2007; however, after a long wait and millions of pounds spent on inquiries, the plans were cancelled in May 2016 citing little value for money.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Public transport in the Leeds area is coordinated and developed by <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Metro" title="West Yorkshire Metro">West Yorkshire Metro</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> with service information provided by Leeds City Council<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> and West Yorkshire Metro. The primary means of public transport in Leeds are the bus services. The main provider is <a href="/wiki/First_Leeds" title="First Leeds">First Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Yorkshire" title="Arriva Yorkshire">Arriva Yorkshire</a> serves routes to the south of the city. Leeds City bus station is at Dyer Street and is used by bus services to towns and cities in Yorkshire, plus a small number of local services. Adjacent to it is the coach station for <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> coach services. Buses out of the city are mainly provided by First Leeds and Arriva Yorkshire. <a href="/wiki/Harrogate_Bus_Company" title="Harrogate Bus Company">Harrogate Bus Company</a> provides a service to <a href="/wiki/Harrogate" title="Harrogate">Harrogate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ripon" title="Ripon">Ripon</a>. <a href="/wiki/Keighley_Bus_Company" title="Keighley Bus Company">Keighley Bus Company</a> provides a service to <a href="/wiki/Shipley,_West_Yorkshire" title="Shipley, West Yorkshire">Shipley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bingley" title="Bingley">Bingley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keighley" title="Keighley">Keighley</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Coastliner" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Coastliner">Yorkshire Coastliner</a> service runs from Leeds to <a href="/wiki/Bridlington" title="Bridlington">Bridlington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filey" title="Filey">Filey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_North_Yorkshire" title="Scarborough, North Yorkshire">Scarborough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whitby" title="Whitby">Whitby</a> via <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malton,_North_Yorkshire" title="Malton, North Yorkshire">Malton</a>. <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_in_Hull" title="Stagecoach in Hull">Stagecoach</a> provides a service to <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a> via <a href="/wiki/Goole" title="Goole">Goole</a>.\n</p><p>From <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds railway station</a> at New Station Street, <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Metro" title="West Yorkshire Metro">West Yorkshire Metro</a> trains operated by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> run to Leeds\' suburbs and onwards to all parts of Leeds City Region. The station is one of the busiest in England outside London, with over 900 trains and 50,000 passengers passing through every day.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> It provides national and international connections as well as services to local and regional destinations. The station itself has 17 platforms, making it the largest in England outside London.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bradford_Airport" title="Leeds Bradford Airport">Leeds Bradford International Airport</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Yeadon,_West_Yorkshire" title="Yeadon, West Yorkshire">Yeadon</a>, about 10 miles (16&#160;km) to the north-west of the city centre, and has both charter and scheduled flights to destinations within Europe plus Egypt, Tunisia, Turkey and the USA. There is a direct rail service from Leeds to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a>; however, there isn\'t one to the nearby Leeds Bradford Airport. <a href="/wiki/Humberside_Airport" title="Humberside Airport">Humberside Airport</a> is 70 miles (113&#160;km) east of Leeds.\n</p><p>The city and metropolitan borough of Leeds is served by 16 railway stations and there are plans to open several more within the next 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">Recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterloo_Lake_Roundhay_07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Waterloo_Lake_Roundhay_07.jpg/220px-Waterloo_Lake_Roundhay_07.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Waterloo_Lake_Roundhay_07.jpg/330px-Waterloo_Lake_Roundhay_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Waterloo_Lake_Roundhay_07.jpg/440px-Waterloo_Lake_Roundhay_07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1917" data-file-height="1287" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterloo_Lake_Roundhay_07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Waterloo Lake in <a href="/wiki/Roundhay_Park" title="Roundhay Park">Roundhay Park</a>, one of the largest urban parks in Europe</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Temple_Newsam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Temple_Newsam.jpg/220px-Temple_Newsam.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Temple_Newsam.jpg/330px-Temple_Newsam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Temple_Newsam.jpg/440px-Temple_Newsam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2513" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Temple_Newsam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Mansion at <a href="/wiki/Temple_Newsam" title="Temple Newsam">Temple Newsam</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Walking">Walking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Walking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Country_Way" title="Leeds Country Way">Leeds Country Way</a> is a waymarked circular walk of 62 miles (100&#160;km) through the rural outskirts of the city, never more than 7 miles (11&#160;km) from <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Square" title="Leeds City Square">City Square</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Meanwood_Valley_Trail" title="Meanwood Valley Trail">Meanwood Valley Trail</a> leads from <a href="/wiki/Woodhouse_Moor" title="Woodhouse Moor">Woodhouse Moor</a> along <a href="/wiki/Meanwood_Beck" title="Meanwood Beck">Meanwood Beck</a> to <a href="/wiki/Golden_Acre_Park" title="Golden Acre Park">Golden Acre Park</a>. The Leeds extension of the <a href="/wiki/Dales_Way" title="Dales Way">Dales Way</a> follows the Meanwood Valley Trail before it branches off to head towards <a href="/wiki/Ilkley" title="Ilkley">Ilkley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windermere" title="Windermere">Windermere</a>. Leeds is on the northern section of the <a href="/wiki/Trans_Pennine_Trail" title="Trans Pennine Trail">Trans Pennine Trail</a> for walkers and cyclists, and the towpath of the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Liverpool_Canal" title="Leeds and Liverpool Canal">Leeds and Liverpool Canal</a> is another popular walking and cycling route. <a href="/wiki/The_White_Rose_Way" title="The White Rose Way">The White Rose Way</a> walking trail to <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_North_Yorkshire" title="Scarborough, North Yorkshire">Scarborough</a> begins at City Square. In addition, there are many parks and public footpaths in both the urban and rural parts of Leeds, and <a href="/wiki/The_Ramblers" title="The Ramblers">The Ramblers</a>\' Association, <a href="/wiki/Youth_Hostels_Association_(England_%26_Wales)" title="Youth Hostels Association (England &amp; Wales)">YHA</a> and other walking organisations offer sociable walks. The Ramblers\' Association publish various booklets of walks in and around Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_open_spaces">Parks and open spaces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Parks and open spaces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Leeds has many large parks and open spaces. <a href="/wiki/Roundhay_Park" title="Roundhay Park">Roundhay Park</a> is the largest park in the city, and is one of the largest city parks in Europe. The park has more than 700 acres (2.8&#160;km<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> of parkland, lakes, woodland and gardens which are all owned by Leeds City Council. Other parks in the city include: Beckett Park, Bramley Fall Park, Cross Flatts Park, East End Park, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Acre_Park" title="Golden Acre Park">Golden Acre Park</a>, Gotts Park,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> the gardens and grounds of <a href="/wiki/Harewood_House" title="Harewood House">Harewood House</a>, Horforth Hall Park, Meanwood Park, <a href="/wiki/Middleton_Park" title="Middleton Park">Middleton Park</a>, Potternewton Park, Pudsey Park,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Temple_Newsam" title="Temple Newsam">Temple Newsam</a>, Western Flatts Park and <a href="/wiki/Woodhouse_Moor" title="Woodhouse Moor">Woodhouse Moor</a>. There are many more smaller parks and open spaces scattered around the city, which makes Leeds one of the greenest cities in the United Kingdom in a 2017 survey. Leeds was ranked at number seven, just behind Sheffield, but ahead of Bradford, Manchester and Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Leeds" title="List of schools in Leeds">List of schools in Leeds</a></div>\n<p>At the time of the 2001 census Leeds had a population of 183,000 young people aged 0\xe2\x80\x9319 of whom 110,000 were attending local authority schools.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In 2008 Education Leeds, a non-profit company owned by Leeds City Council, provided for 220 primary schools, 39 secondary schools and 6 special inclusive learning centres.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Under the government <a href="/wiki/Building_Schools_for_the_Future" title="Building Schools for the Future">Building Schools for the Future</a> initiative, Leeds secured \xc2\xa3260m, to transform 13 secondary schools into high achieving, e-confident, inclusive schools. The first three of these schools at <a href="/wiki/Allerton_High_School" title="Allerton High School">Allerton High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pudsey_Grangefield_School" title="Pudsey Grangefield School">Pudsey Grangefield School</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Rodillian_Academy" title="The Rodillian Academy">Rodillian School</a>, were opened in September 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The demand for primary school places in Leeds has recently hit a 15-year peak, with an estimated 10,500 new starters this year.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s oldest and largest private school is the <a href="/wiki/Grammar_School_at_Leeds" title="Grammar School at Leeds">Grammar School at Leeds</a>, which was legally re-created in 2005 following the merger of <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Grammar_School" title="Leeds Grammar School">Leeds Grammar School</a>, established 1552, and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Girls%27_High_School" title="Leeds Girls&#39; High School">Leeds Girls\' High School</a>, established 1876. Other independent schools in Leeds include faith schools serving the Jewish<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> and Muslim<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> communities.\n</p><p>Leeds was one of a number of local authorities to try the <a href="/wiki/Three-tier_education" title="Three-tier education">three-tier system</a> with first, middle and secondary schools. It reverted to the two-tier system in 1992.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_and_higher_education">Further and higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Further and higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parkinson_Building,_Leeds_University,_England-12Sept2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Parkinson_Building%2C_Leeds_University%2C_England-12Sept2010.jpg/220px-Parkinson_Building%2C_Leeds_University%2C_England-12Sept2010.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Parkinson_Building%2C_Leeds_University%2C_England-12Sept2010.jpg/330px-Parkinson_Building%2C_Leeds_University%2C_England-12Sept2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Parkinson_Building%2C_Leeds_University%2C_England-12Sept2010.jpg/440px-Parkinson_Building%2C_Leeds_University%2C_England-12Sept2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2104" data-file-height="1528" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parkinson_Building,_Leeds_University,_England-12Sept2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Parkinson_Building" title="Parkinson Building">Parkinson Building</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">University of Leeds</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Broadcasting_Tower,_Leeds,_West_Yorkshire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Broadcasting_Tower%2C_Leeds%2C_West_Yorkshire.jpg/220px-Broadcasting_Tower%2C_Leeds%2C_West_Yorkshire.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Broadcasting_Tower%2C_Leeds%2C_West_Yorkshire.jpg/330px-Broadcasting_Tower%2C_Leeds%2C_West_Yorkshire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Broadcasting_Tower%2C_Leeds%2C_West_Yorkshire.jpg/440px-Broadcasting_Tower%2C_Leeds%2C_West_Yorkshire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3672" data-file-height="4896" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Broadcasting_Tower,_Leeds,_West_Yorkshire.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Broadcasting Tower at the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Beckett_University" title="Leeds Beckett University">Leeds Beckett University</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">Further education</a> in Leeds is provided by <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_College" title="Leeds City College">Leeds City College</a> (formed by a merger in 2009 and having over 60,000 students), <a href="/wiki/Leeds_College_of_Building" title="Leeds College of Building">Leeds College of Building</a>, <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Catholic_Sixth_Form_College" title="Notre Dame Catholic Sixth Form College">Notre Dame Catholic Sixth Form College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Hudson_College" title="Elliott Hudson College">Elliott Hudson College</a>. The city has five universities: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">University of Leeds</a>\xe2\x80\x94which received its charter in 1904 having developed from the Yorkshire College which was founded in 1874 and the Leeds School of Medicine of 1831; <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Beckett_University" title="Leeds Beckett University">Leeds Beckett University</a> (formerly Leeds Polytechnic) which became a university in 1992 but can trace its roots to the <a href="/wiki/Mechanics%27_Institutes" title="Mechanics&#39; Institutes">Mechanics\' Institute</a> of 1824; <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Trinity_University" title="Leeds Trinity University">Leeds Trinity University</a> which began in 1966 as two teacher training colleges which merged in 1980 to form Trinity and All Saints College and became a university in 2012; the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Law" title="University of Law">University of Law</a> (formerly the College of Law) which became a university in 2012 and moved to its current Leeds centre campus from <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a> in 2014; and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Arts_University" title="Leeds Arts University">Leeds Arts University</a>, which was founded in 1846 as the Leeds School of Art, and became a university in 2017.\n</p><p>The University of Leeds has about 31,000 students, of which 21,500 are full-time or sandwich undergraduate degree students,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Leeds Beckett University has 25,805<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> students of which 12,000 are full-time or sandwich undergraduate degree students and 2,100 full-time or sandwich HND students.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Leeds Trinity University has just under 3,000 students,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Other higher education establishments are: <a href="/wiki/Leeds_College_of_Music" title="Leeds College of Music">Leeds College of Music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_School_of_Contemporary_Dance" title="Northern School of Contemporary Dance">Northern School of Contemporary Dance</a>. The city was voted the Best UK University Destination by a survey in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-cug_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cug-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Leeds" title="Culture of Leeds">Culture of Leeds</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds._Henry_Moore_town_-_geograph.org.uk_-_353135.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Leeds._Henry_Moore_town_-_geograph.org.uk_-_353135.jpg/220px-Leeds._Henry_Moore_town_-_geograph.org.uk_-_353135.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Leeds._Henry_Moore_town_-_geograph.org.uk_-_353135.jpg/330px-Leeds._Henry_Moore_town_-_geograph.org.uk_-_353135.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Leeds._Henry_Moore_town_-_geograph.org.uk_-_353135.jpg/440px-Leeds._Henry_Moore_town_-_geograph.org.uk_-_353135.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="442" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds._Henry_Moore_town_-_geograph.org.uk_-_353135.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Henry Moore Statue outside <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Art_Gallery" title="Leeds Art Gallery">Leeds Art Gallery</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Although the city\'s municipal art gallery did not open until 1888, the history of art practise and collecting has a long history in Leeds. <a href="/wiki/J._M._W._Turner" title="J. M. W. Turner">J. M. W. Turner</a> painted numerous scenes in and around the city,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and the city was home to one of Britain\'s largest collections of Pre-Raphaelite Art, owned by Thomas Plint, during the nineteenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> There was also an early history of holding large-scale public exhibitions in the city, most notably the series of \'Polytechnic Exhibitions\' held regularly from 1839.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds produced many notable artists and sculptors, including <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Armitage" title="Kenneth Armitage">Kenneth Armitage</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Atkinson_Grimshaw" title="John Atkinson Grimshaw">John Atkinson Grimshaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Kramer" title="Jacob Kramer">Jacob Kramer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Hepworth" title="Barbara Hepworth">Barbara Hepworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore" title="Henry Moore">Henry Moore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Wadsworth" title="Edward Wadsworth">Edward Wadsworth</a>, and was the centre for a particularly radical strain of British art. Before the First World War Leeds was the home of an unusual modernist arts organisation, called the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Arts_Club" title="Leeds Arts Club">Leeds Arts Club</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Richard_Orage" title="Alfred Richard Orage">Alfred Orage</a>, which lasted from 1903 to 1923. Notable members included <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Kramer" title="Jacob Kramer">Jacob Kramer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Read" title="Herbert Read">Herbert Read</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rutter" title="Frank Rutter">Frank Rutter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Sadler_(educationist)" title="Michael Sadler (educationist)">Michael Sadler</a>. As well as advocating a radical political agenda, supporting the <a href="/wiki/Suffragette" title="Suffragette">Suffragettes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Labour_Party" title="Independent Labour Party">Independent Labour Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Society" title="Fabian Society">Fabian Society</a>, and promoting the philosophy of <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Nietzsche" title="Friedrich Nietzsche">Friedrich Nietzsche</a>, the Leeds Arts Club was almost unique in Britain as being an exponent of <a href="/wiki/German_Expressionism" title="German Expressionism">German Expressionist</a> ideas about art and culture. As a result, it staged very early British exhibitions of work by European expressionist artists, such as <a href="/wiki/Wassily_Kandinsky" title="Wassily Kandinsky">Wassily Kandinsky</a>, showing their work in the city as early as 1913,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> and produced its own English Expressionist artists, including Jacob Kramer and Bruce Turner.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1920s Leeds College of Art was the starting point for the careers of the sculptors <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Hepworth" title="Barbara Hepworth">Barbara Hepworth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore" title="Henry Moore">Henry Moore</a>, and in the 1950s, and 1960s it was one of the leading centres for radical art education in Britain under the guidance of artists such as <a href="/wiki/Harry_Thubron" title="Harry Thubron">Harry Thubron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hudson_(painter)" title="Thomas Hudson (painter)">Tom Hudson</a>, and the art historian <a href="/wiki/Norbert_Lynton" title="Norbert Lynton">Norbert Lynton</a>. Their attempts to redefine what art education should mean in the post-<a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a> period led the artist <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Heron" title="Patrick Heron">Patrick Heron</a> to claim in 1971 in <i>The Guardian</i> newspaper that "Leeds is the most influential art school in Europe since the <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">Bauhaus</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> This willingness to push at the boundaries of acceptable public behaviour from artists was also evident in 1966 when Leeds College of Art staged an exhibition of paintings by the Cypriot artist <a href="/wiki/Stass_Paraskos" title="Stass Paraskos">Stass Paraskos</a>, who taught at the College, which was raided by the police after allegations of obscenity.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This radicalism continued into the 1970s when the higher education component of Leeds College of Art was split from the college to form the nucleus of the new multidisciplinary Leeds Polytechnic, now called <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Beckett_University" title="Leeds Beckett University">Leeds Beckett University</a>. Performance art had been taught earlier at Leeds College of Art, notably by the <a href="/wiki/Fluxus" title="Fluxus">Fluxus</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Robin_Page" title="Robin Page">Robin Page</a> during his time as a tutor there in the mid-1960s, but in 1977 a performance art work hit the national news headlines when the students Pete Parkin and Derek Wain used an air pistol to shoot a line up of live <a href="/wiki/Budgerigar" title="Budgerigar">budgerigars</a> in front of an audience at Leeds Polytechnic.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">University of Leeds</a> was the <i>alma mater</i> of <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Read" title="Herbert Read">Herbert Read</a>, one of the leading international theorists of modern art from the mid-twentieth century,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> and also the teaching base for the <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxist</a> art historian <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Hauser" title="Arnold Hauser">Arnold Hauser</a> from 1951 to 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Partly due to Herbert Read\'s connection with the University, from 1950 to 1970 the University was the host of one of the first <a href="/wiki/Artist-in-residence" title="Artist-in-residence">artist-in-residence</a> schemes in Britain, using funding from the then owner of <a href="/wiki/Ashgate_Publishing" title="Ashgate Publishing">Lund Humphries</a> books, Peter Gregory. The Gregory Fellowships, as the residencies were known, were given to painters and sculptors for up to two years to allow them to develop their own work and influence the University in any way they saw fit. Amongst those holding the fellowships were <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Armitage" title="Kenneth Armitage">Kenneth Armitage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reg_Butler" title="Reg Butler">Reg Butler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Creffield" title="Dennis Creffield">Dennis Creffield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terry_Frost" title="Terry Frost">Terry Frost</a> and others. Parallel Gregory Fellowships also existed in music and poetry at the University.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds was also a centre for radical feminist art, with one of the first galleries in Britain dedicated to showing the work of women photographers, the Pavilion Gallery, opening in the city in 1983, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">University of Leeds</a> School of Fine Art being a well-known centre for the development of feminist art history, under <a href="/wiki/Griselda_Pollock" title="Griselda Pollock">Griselda Pollock</a>, during the 1980s and 1990s. Possibly as a result of the strength of feminist art in Leeds, in November 1984 an exhibition of ceramics by students and staff at Leeds Polytechnic was attacked by a group of feminist activists who destroyed eight sculptures on display which they deemed to be degrading to women.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The University of Leeds\'s School of Fine Art also specialised in <a href="/wiki/Art_%26_Language" title="Art &amp; Language">Art &amp; Language</a> conceptual art practice, under <a href="/wiki/Terry_Atkinson" title="Terry Atkinson">Terry Atkinson</a>, again in the 1980s and 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A major sculpture research centre and gallery, the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore_Foundation" title="Henry Moore Foundation">Henry Moore Institute</a>, is located alongside <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Art_Gallery" title="Leeds Art Gallery">Leeds Art Gallery</a> in the city centre, and in 2013 a new contemporary art centre, called <a href="/wiki/The_Tetley_(Leeds)" title="The Tetley (Leeds)">The Tetley</a>, opened on the site of the former Tetley Brewery to the south of the city centre.\n</p><p>In March 2017, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> voted Leeds as the number one cultural place to live in Britain. This was ahead of London, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Ives,_Cornwall" title="St Ives, Cornwall">St Ives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stratford-upon-Avon" title="Stratford-upon-Avon">Stratford-upon-Avon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham" title="Cheltenham">Cheltenham</a>. The citation notes that Leeds has <a href="/wiki/Opera_North" title="Opera North">Opera North</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ballet" title="Northern Ballet">Northern Ballet</a>, the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Playhouse" class="mw-redirect" title="West Yorkshire Playhouse">West Yorkshire Playhouse</a> amongst may other attractions that ranked it at number one.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carnivals_and_festivals">Carnivals and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Carnivals and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_West_Indian_Carnival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Leeds_West_Indian_Carnival.jpg/220px-Leeds_West_Indian_Carnival.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Leeds_West_Indian_Carnival.jpg/330px-Leeds_West_Indian_Carnival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Leeds_West_Indian_Carnival.jpg/440px-Leeds_West_Indian_Carnival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_West_Indian_Carnival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Carnival" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds Carnival">Leeds Carnival</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_West_Indian_Carnival" title="Leeds West Indian Carnival">Leeds Carnival</a> is Western Europe\'s oldest West Indian Carnival, and the UK\'s third-largest after the Notting Hill and Nottingham Carnival.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> It attracts around 100,000 people over 2 days to the streets of Chapeltown and Harehills. There is a large procession that finishes at Potternewton Park, where there are stalls, entertainment and refreshments. The <a href="/wiki/Reading_and_Leeds_Festivals" title="Reading and Leeds Festivals">Leeds Festival</a>, featuring some of the biggest names in rock and indie music, takes place every year in <a href="/wiki/Bramham_Park" title="Bramham Park">Bramham Park</a>. The Leeds Asian Festival, formerly the Leeds <a href="/wiki/Mela" title="Mela">Mela</a>, is held in Roundhay Park.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Otley" title="Otley">Otley</a> Folk Festival (patron: <a href="/wiki/Nic_Jones" title="Nic Jones">Nic Jones</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Walking Festival,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Carnival<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> and Victorian Christmas Fayre<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> are annual events. <a href="/wiki/Light_Night" title="Light Night">Light Night</a> Leeds takes place each October,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> and many venues in the city are open to the public for <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Open_Days" title="Heritage Open Days">Heritage Open Days</a> in September.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_International_Piano_Competition" title="Leeds International Piano Competition">Leeds International Pianoforte Competition</a>, established in 1963 by <a href="/wiki/Fanny_Waterman" title="Fanny Waterman">Fanny Waterman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marion_Stein" title="Marion Stein">Marion Stein</a>, has been held in the city every three years since 1963 and has launched the careers of many major concert pianists. The Leeds International Concert Season, which includes orchestral and choral concerts in <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Town_Hall" title="Leeds Town Hall">Leeds Town Hall</a> and other events, is the largest local authority music programme in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_International_Film_Festival" title="Leeds International Film Festival">Leeds International Film Festival</a> is the largest film festival in England outside London<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> and shows films from around the world. It incorporates the highly successful <i>Leeds Young People\'s Film Festival</i>, which features exciting and innovative films made both for and by children and young people.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Garforth" title="Garforth">Garforth</a> is host to the fortnight-long festival The <a href="/wiki/Garforth_Arts_Festival" title="Garforth Arts Festival">Garforth Arts Festival</a> which has been an annual event since 2005. The <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Allerton" title="Chapel Allerton">Chapel Allerton</a> Arts Festival is a week-long music and arts event starting in 1998 and held the week after August Bank Holiday each year.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Festival_Fringe" title="Leeds Festival Fringe">Leeds Festival Fringe</a> is a week long-music festival created in 2010 to showcase local talent in the week prior to <a href="/wiki/Reading_and_Leeds_Festivals" title="Reading and Leeds Festivals">Leeds Festival</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_Le_Prince.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Louis_Le_Prince.jpg/220px-Louis_Le_Prince.jpg" width="220" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Louis_Le_Prince.jpg/330px-Louis_Le_Prince.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/Louis_Le_Prince.jpg 2x" data-file-width="363" data-file-height="454" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_Le_Prince.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Louis_Le_Prince" title="Louis Le Prince">Louis Le Prince</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In October 1888 <a href="/wiki/Louis_Le_Prince" title="Louis Le Prince">Louis Le Prince</a> filmed moving picture sequences <i><a href="/wiki/Roundhay_Garden_Scene" title="Roundhay Garden Scene">Roundhay Garden Scene</a></i> and a <i><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bridge" title="Leeds Bridge">Leeds Bridge</a></i> street scene using his single-lens camera and <a href="/wiki/Kodak" title="Kodak">Eastman</a>\'s paper film.<sup id="cite_ref-nationalmediamuseum_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalmediamuseum-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> These were several years before the work of competing inventors such as <a href="/wiki/Auguste_and_Louis_Lumi%C3%A8re" title="Auguste and Louis Lumi\xc3\xa8re">Auguste and Louis Lumi\xc3\xa8re</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Thomas Edison</a>.\nToday, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_International_Film_Festival" title="Leeds International Film Festival">Leeds International Film Festival</a>\'s International Short Film Competition is named after Louis Le Prince.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The 2015 documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/The_First_Film" title="The First Film">The First Film</a></i>, which first aired at the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_International_Film_Festival" title="Edinburgh International Film Festival">Edinburgh International Film Festival</a>, documents Le Prince\'s pioneering status.<sup id="cite_ref-youngs_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youngs-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wordsworth_Donisthorpe" title="Wordsworth Donisthorpe">Wordsworth Donisthorpe</a> who was also from Leeds, filmed the second-oldest-surviving film. It is not known if he and Louis Le Prince ever met but they both had a strong connection to the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Philosophical_and_Literary_Society" title="Leeds Philosophical and Literary Society">Leeds Philosophical and Literary Society</a>. Donisthorpe\'s patent for a camera to capture the moving image pre dated Le Prince\'s by twelve years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Leeds has a rich film exhibition culture. In addition to the Leeds International Film Festival and Leeds Young Film Festival, the city hosts numerous independent cinemas and pop-up venues for film screenings.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Cottage_Road_Cinema" title="The Cottage Road Cinema">The Cottage Road Cinema</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park_Picture_House,_Leeds" title="Hyde Park Picture House, Leeds">Hyde Park Picture House</a> have continuously been showing films since 1912 and 1914, respectively, which ranks them among the oldest still-running cinemas in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Television_shows_set_in_Leeds" title="Category:Television shows set in Leeds">Category:Television shows set in Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Films_set_in_Leeds" title="Category:Films set in Leeds">Category:Films set in Leeds</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_Yorkshire,_Leeds_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1026004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A quirky modern five-storey building with a large sign saying &quot;BBC Yorkshire&quot; in black above the second-floor windows on the white-fronted fa\xc3\xa7ade of the lower four floors can be seen on the far side of a dual-carriageway road with a barrier along the central reservation. At right-angles to the right of the building is a tall blue slab with the letters &quot;BBC&quot; in white at the top. The left side of the building is mostly brick-red with a few windows, but above it is a light blue windowless section. The roof above this and the grey fifth floor of the frontage curves gently down to the rear. A lone car is driving from left to right along the road; between it and the building, temporary boards have been erected in front of a building to the left. In the top left-hand corner of the picture, part of a tall many-windowed building can be seen." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/BBC_Yorkshire%2C_Leeds_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1026004.jpg/220px-BBC_Yorkshire%2C_Leeds_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1026004.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/BBC_Yorkshire%2C_Leeds_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1026004.jpg/330px-BBC_Yorkshire%2C_Leeds_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1026004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/BBC_Yorkshire%2C_Leeds_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1026004.jpg/440px-BBC_Yorkshire%2C_Leeds_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1026004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="383" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC_Yorkshire,_Leeds_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1026004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/BBC_Yorkshire" title="BBC Yorkshire">BBC Yorkshire</a> studios</div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Post_Newspapers" title="Yorkshire Post Newspapers">Yorkshire Post Newspapers</a> Ltd, owned by <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Press" title="Johnston Press">Johnston Press</a> plc, is based in the city, and produces a daily morning broadsheet, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Yorkshire_Post" title="The Yorkshire Post">The Yorkshire Post</a></i>, and an evening paper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Evening_Post" title="Yorkshire Evening Post">Yorkshire Evening Post</a></i> (YEP). The YEP has a website which includes a series of community pages which focus on specific areas of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Wetherby_News" title="Wetherby News">Wetherby News</a></i> covers mainly areas within the north eastern sector of the district, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Gazette_%26_Observer" title="Gazette &amp; Observer">Wharfedale &amp; Airedale Observer</a></i>, published in <a href="/wiki/Ilkley" title="Ilkley">Ilkley</a>, covers the north west, both appearing weekly. The two largest universities both have <a href="/wiki/Student_publication" title="Student publication">student newspapers</a>, the weekly <i><a href="/wiki/The_Gryphon" title="The Gryphon">Leeds Student</a></i> from the University of Leeds and the monthly <i><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Beckett_Students%27_Union" title="Leeds Beckett Students&#39; Union">The Met</a></i> from Leeds Beckett University. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Leeds_Guide" title="The Leeds Guide">The Leeds Guide</a></i> was a fortnightly listings magazine, which was established in 1997 and ceased publication in 2012. Free publications include the <i>Leeds Weekly News</i>, produced by Yorkshire Post Newspapers in four geographic versions and distributed to households in the main urban area of the city,<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> and the regional version of <i><a href="/wiki/Metro_(British_newspaper)" title="Metro (British newspaper)">Metro</a></i> which is distributed on buses and at railway stations.\n</p><p>Regional television and radio stations have bases in the city; <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> Television and <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> both have regional studios and broadcasting centres in Leeds. <a href="/wiki/ITV_Yorkshire" title="ITV Yorkshire">ITV Yorkshire</a>, formerly Yorkshire Television, broadcasts from <a href="/wiki/The_Leeds_Studios" title="The Leeds Studios">the Leeds Studios</a> on Kirkstall Road.
