There are a number of independent film production companies, including the not-for-profit cooperative Leeds Animation Workshop, founded in 1978; community video producers Vera Media and several small commercial production companies. <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Leeds" title="BBC Radio Leeds">BBC Radio Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Aire" title="Radio Aire">Radio Aire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magic_828" class="mw-redirect" title="Magic 828">Magic 828</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_Yorkshire" title="Capital Yorkshire">Capital Yorkshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Real_Radio_(Yorkshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Radio (Yorkshire)">Real Radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Radio" title="Yorkshire Radio">Yorkshire Radio</a> broadcast from the city. <a href="/wiki/LSRfm.com" class="mw-redirect" title="LSRfm.com">LSRfm.com</a>, is based in <a href="/wiki/Leeds_University_Union" title="Leeds University Union">Leeds University Union</a>, and regularly hosts outside broadcasts around the city. Many communities within Leeds now have their own local radio stations, such as <a href="/wiki/East_Leeds_FM" title="East Leeds FM">East Leeds FM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tempo_FM" title="Tempo FM">Tempo FM</a> for <a href="/wiki/Wetherby" title="Wetherby">Wetherby</a> and the surrounding areas.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Made_in_Leeds" class="mw-redirect" title="Made in Leeds">Made in Leeds</a> is a local television station which launched across the city in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> A privately owned television station: Leeds Television is run by volunteers and supported by professionals in the media industry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Armouries_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Royal_Armouries_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg/220px-Royal_Armouries_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg" width="220" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Royal_Armouries_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg/330px-Royal_Armouries_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Royal_Armouries_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg/440px-Royal_Armouries_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3242" data-file-height="3062" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Armouries_Leeds_West_Yorkshire.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Royal_Armouries_Museum_(Leeds)" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Armouries Museum (Leeds)">Royal Armouries Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds-city-museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Leeds-city-museum.jpg/220px-Leeds-city-museum.jpg" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Leeds-city-museum.jpg/330px-Leeds-city-museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Leeds-city-museum.jpg/440px-Leeds-city-museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="534" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds-city-museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Museum" title="Leeds City Museum">Leeds City Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_Museum_Discovery_Centre_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Leeds_Museum_Discovery_Centre_2017.jpg/220px-Leeds_Museum_Discovery_Centre_2017.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Leeds_Museum_Discovery_Centre_2017.jpg/330px-Leeds_Museum_Discovery_Centre_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Leeds_Museum_Discovery_Centre_2017.jpg/440px-Leeds_Museum_Discovery_Centre_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_Museum_Discovery_Centre_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leeds Museum Discovery Centre</div></div></div>\n<p>A new <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Museum" title="Leeds City Museum">Leeds City Museum</a> opened in 2008<sup id="cite_ref-citymuseum_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citymuseum-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Square,_Leeds" title="Millennium Square, Leeds">Millennium Square</a>. <a href="/wiki/Abbey_House_Museum" title="Abbey House Museum">Abbey House Museum</a> is housed in the former gatehouse of <a href="/wiki/Kirkstall_Abbey" title="Kirkstall Abbey">Kirkstall Abbey</a>, and includes walk-through Victorian streets and galleries describing the history of the abbey, childhood, and Victorian Leeds. <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Industrial_Museum_at_Armley_Mills" title="Leeds Industrial Museum at Armley Mills">Armley Mills Industrial Museum</a> is housed in what was once the world\'s largest woollen mill,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> and includes industrial machinery and railway locomotives. This museum also shows the first known moving pictures in the world which were taken in the city, by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Le_Prince" title="Louis Le Prince">Louis Le Prince</a>, of a <i><a href="/wiki/Roundhay_Garden_Scene" title="Roundhay Garden Scene">Roundhay Garden Scene</a></i> and of <i><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bridge" title="Leeds Bridge">Leeds Bridge</a></i> in 1888. These short film clips can be found on YouTube.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Thwaite_Mills" title="Thwaite Mills">Thwaite Mills</a> Watermill Museum is a fully restored 1820s water-powered mill on the <a href="/wiki/River_Aire" title="River Aire">River Aire</a> to the east of the city centre. The <a href="/wiki/Thackray_Medical_Museum" title="Thackray Medical Museum">Thackray Museum</a> is a museum of the history of medicine, featuring topics such as Victorian public health, pre-anaesthesia surgery, and safety in childbirth. It is housed in a former <a href="/wiki/Workhouse" title="Workhouse">workhouse</a> next to <a href="/wiki/St_James%27s_University_Hospital" title="St James&#39;s University Hospital">St James\'s Hospital</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Armouries_Museum" title="Royal Armouries Museum">Royal Armouries Museum</a> opened in 1996 in a dramatic modern building when this part of the national collection was transferred from the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a>. Nearby is the Leeds Museum Discovery Centre (formerly housed at the Leeds Museum Resource Centre in <a href="/wiki/Yeadon,_West_Yorkshire" title="Yeadon, West Yorkshire">Yeadon</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-NatArch_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatArch-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> the major storage of items not currently on display in museums, and open to the public by appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-NatArch_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatArch-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Discovery_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Discovery-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Art_Gallery" title="Leeds Art Gallery">Leeds Art Gallery</a> houses important collections of traditional and contemporary British art. It is closed for refurbishment until 13 October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-LAG_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAG-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Smaller museums in Leeds include <a href="/wiki/Otley_Museum" title="Otley Museum">Otley Museum</a>; <a href="/wiki/Horsforth" title="Horsforth">Horsforth</a> Village Museum;<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> ULITA, an Archive of International Textiles;<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and the museum at <a href="/wiki/Fulneck_Moravian_Settlement" title="Fulneck Moravian Settlement">Fulneck Moravian Settlement</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Music.2C_theatre_and_dance"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Music,_theatre_and_dance">Music, theatre and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Music, theatre and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_in_Leeds" title="Music in Leeds">Music in Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_bands_originating_in_Leeds" title="List of bands originating in Leeds">List of bands originating in Leeds</a></div>\n<p>Leeds is home to the refurbished <a href="/wiki/Grand_Theatre,_Leeds" title="Grand Theatre, Leeds">Grand Theatre</a> where the only national opera company outside London, <a href="/wiki/Opera_North" title="Opera North">Opera North</a>, is based.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Varieties" title="Leeds City Varieties">City Varieties</a> Music Hall is one of the UK\'s few remaining music halls, and famously hosted performances by <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">Charlie Chaplin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Houdini" title="Harry Houdini">Harry Houdini</a>. It was also the venue of the BBC television programme <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Old_Days_(UK_TV_series)" title="The Good Old Days (UK TV series)">The Good Old Days</a></i>. The newest theatre, containing two auditoriums, is the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Playhouse" title="Leeds Playhouse">Leeds Playhouse</a>, which had formerly been known as the West Yorkshire Playhouse.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Just south of <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bridge" title="Leeds Bridge">Leeds Bridge</a> once stood <a href="/wiki/The_Theatre,_Leeds" title="The Theatre, Leeds">The Theatre</a> which hosted <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Siddons" title="Sarah Siddons">Sarah Siddons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ching_Lau_Lauro" title="Ching Lau Lauro">Ching Lau Lauro</a> in 1786 and 1834, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Leodis_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leodis-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Playbill_22_Sep_1834_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playbill_22_Sep_1834-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds is also home to <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Dance_Theatre" title="Phoenix Dance Theatre">Phoenix Dance Theatre</a>, who were formed in the Harehills area of the city in 1981, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ballet_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ballet Theatre">Northern Ballet Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> In autumn 2010 the two companies moved into a purpose-built dance centre which is the largest space for dance outside London. It is also the only space for dance to house a national classical and a national contemporary dance company alongside each another.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/First_Direct_Arena" title="First Direct Arena">First Direct Arena</a><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> opened in September 2013. The 13,500-seater stadium is rapidly becoming the city\'s number one venue for live music, indoor sports and many other events. Concerts are also held at the O2 Academy, Elland Road, which has hosted groups such as Queen and Kaiser Chiefs, among others and at the universities. <a href="/wiki/Roundhay_Park" title="Roundhay Park">Roundhay Park</a> in north Leeds has seen some of the world\'s biggest artists including <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Williams" title="Robbie Williams">Robbie Williams</a>.\n</p><p>Popular musical acts originating from Leeds include <a href="/wiki/Soft_Cell" title="Soft Cell">Soft Cell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaiser_Chiefs" title="Kaiser Chiefs">Kaiser Chiefs</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Pigeon_Detectives" title="The Pigeon Detectives">The Pigeon Detectives</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Wedding_Present" title="The Wedding Present">The Wedding Present</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Sunshine_Underground" title="The Sunshine Underground">The Sunshine Underground</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Sisters_of_Mercy" title="The Sisters of Mercy">The Sisters of Mercy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hadouken!" title="Hadouken!">Hadouken!</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corinne_Bailey_Rae" title="Corinne Bailey Rae">Corinne Bailey Rae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur_Pile-Up" title="Dinosaur Pile-Up">Dinosaur Pile-Up</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulled_Apart_by_Horses" title="Pulled Apart by Horses">Pulled Apart by Horses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gang_of_Four_(band)" title="Gang of Four (band)">Gang of Four</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hood_(band)" title="Hood (band)">Hood</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Rhythm_Sisters" title="The Rhythm Sisters">The Rhythm Sisters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah_Saints" title="Utah Saints">Utah Saints</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alt-J" title="Alt-J">Alt-J</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melanie_B" class="mw-redirect" title="Melanie B">Melanie B</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Girls" title="Spice Girls">Spice Girls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Leeds_First_Direct_Arena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/The_Leeds_First_Direct_Arena.jpg/220px-The_Leeds_First_Direct_Arena.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/The_Leeds_First_Direct_Arena.jpg/330px-The_Leeds_First_Direct_Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/The_Leeds_First_Direct_Arena.jpg/440px-The_Leeds_First_Direct_Arena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Leeds_First_Direct_Arena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leeds <a href="/wiki/First_Direct_Arena" title="First Direct Arena">First Direct Arena</a></div></div></div>\n<p>On <a href="/wiki/Valentine%27s_Day" title="Valentine&#39;s Day">Valentine\'s Day</a>, 1970 <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a> performed and recorded their album <i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Leeds" title="Live at Leeds">Live at Leeds</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">Leeds University</a> refectory. Since its initial reception, <i>Live at Leeds</i> has been cited by several <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a> as the best live rock recording of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-cohn_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cohn-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-carr_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carr-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hyden_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hyden-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nightlife">Nightlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Nightlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Leeds has the fourth largest student population in the country (over 200,000<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>), and is therefore one of the UK\'s hotspots for night-life. There are a large number of pubs, bars, nightclubs and restaurants, as well as a multitude of venues for live music. The full range of music tastes is catered for in Leeds. It includes the original home of the famous club nights Back 2 Basics, Speedqueen and <a href="/wiki/Vague_(club)" title="Vague (club)">Vague</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> Morley was the location of <a href="/wiki/Techno" title="Techno">techno</a> club The Orbit.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Leeds has a number of large \'super-clubs\' and there is a selection of independent clubs such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Club_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Club Mission (page does not exist)">Club Mission</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mint_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mint Club (page does not exist)">Mint Club</a>, which is consistently ranked as one of the world\'s best clubs by DJ Magazine. Two other Leeds clubs, The Warehouse and The Garage, featured in the Top 100 Clubs list from 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Leeds has a well established gay nightlife scene. The Bridge Inn and <a href="/wiki/The_New_Penny" title="The New Penny">The New Penny</a>, both on <a href="/wiki/The_Calls" title="The Calls">Call Lane</a>, have long been gay night spots.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Towards <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Square,_Leeds" title="Millennium Square, Leeds">Millennium Square</a> and the Civic or Northern Quarter, is a growing entertainment district providing for both students and weekend visitors. The square has many bars and restaurants and a large outdoor screen. Millennium Square is a venue for large seasonal events such as a <a href="/wiki/Christmas_market" title="Christmas market">Christmas market</a>, gigs and concerts, citywide parties and the Rhythms of the City Festival. It is adjacent to the Mandela Gardens, which were opened by <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> in 2001. A number of public art features, fountains, a canal and greenery can be found here.\n</p><p>Yorkshire has a great history of real ale,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> but several bars near the railway station are fusing traditional beers with a modern bar. Popular bars such as this include The Hop, The Cross Keys and The Brewery Tap.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Leeds" title="Sport in Leeds">Sport in Leeds</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carnegie_Pavilion,_Headingley_Stadium,_Leeds_during_the_second_day_of_the_England-_Sri_Lanka_test_(21st_April_2014)_001.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Carnegie_Pavilion%2C_Headingley_Stadium%2C_Leeds_during_the_second_day_of_the_England-_Sri_Lanka_test_%2821st_April_2014%29_001.JPG/220px-Carnegie_Pavilion%2C_Headingley_Stadium%2C_Leeds_during_the_second_day_of_the_England-_Sri_Lanka_test_%2821st_April_2014%29_001.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Carnegie_Pavilion%2C_Headingley_Stadium%2C_Leeds_during_the_second_day_of_the_England-_Sri_Lanka_test_%2821st_April_2014%29_001.JPG/330px-Carnegie_Pavilion%2C_Headingley_Stadium%2C_Leeds_during_the_second_day_of_the_England-_Sri_Lanka_test_%2821st_April_2014%29_001.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Carnegie_Pavilion%2C_Headingley_Stadium%2C_Leeds_during_the_second_day_of_the_England-_Sri_Lanka_test_%2821st_April_2014%29_001.JPG/440px-Carnegie_Pavilion%2C_Headingley_Stadium%2C_Leeds_during_the_second_day_of_the_England-_Sri_Lanka_test_%2821st_April_2014%29_001.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carnegie_Pavilion,_Headingley_Stadium,_Leeds_during_the_second_day_of_the_England-_Sri_Lanka_test_(21st_April_2014)_001.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Carnegie Pavilion at <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Stadium" title="Headingley Stadium">Headingley Stadium</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elland_Road_Stadium_Leeds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Elland_Road_Stadium_Leeds.jpg/220px-Elland_Road_Stadium_Leeds.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Elland_Road_Stadium_Leeds.jpg/330px-Elland_Road_Stadium_Leeds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Elland_Road_Stadium_Leeds.jpg/440px-Elland_Road_Stadium_Leeds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1945" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elland_Road_Stadium_Leeds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a> Stadium</div></div></div>\n<p>The city has teams representing all the major national sports. <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United F.C.</a> is the city\'s main <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club. <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds Rhinos</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rugby_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League">Rugby League</a>), <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Carnegie" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds Carnegie">Leeds Carnegie</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rugby_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby Union">Rugby Union</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Yorkshire County Cricket Club">Yorkshire County Cricket Club</a> are also based in the city.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> was formed in 1919 and plays at the 37,890-capacity <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a> Stadium in <a href="/wiki/Beeston,_Leeds" title="Beeston, Leeds">Beeston</a>. The team plays in <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">The Championship</a> but has enjoyed success at the highest level in the past, notably during the 1960s, and 1970s when it won two <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">Football League</a> titles, an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>, a <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">Football League Cup</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Inter-Cities_Fairs_Cup" title="Inter-Cities Fairs Cup">Inter-Cities Fairs Cup</a> under the management of <a href="/wiki/Don_Revie" title="Don Revie">Don Revie</a>. The club\'s only other major trophy to date came in 1992 when it won another top division title under the management of <a href="/wiki/Howard_Wilkinson" title="Howard Wilkinson">Howard Wilkinson</a>\xe2\x80\x94the last top division title of the Football League before the creation of the <a href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Premier League">FA Premier League</a>, in which Leeds would play for 12 years before being relegated.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds Rhinos</a> are the most successful <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> team in Leeds. In 2009 they became first club to be <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> champions three seasons running, giving them their fourth Super League title.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\nThey play their home games at the <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Stadium" title="Headingley Stadium">Headingley Carnegie Stadium</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hunslet_R.L.F.C." title="Hunslet R.L.F.C.">Hunslet</a>, based at the <a href="/wiki/John_Charles_Centre_for_Sport" title="John Charles Centre for Sport">John Charles Centre for Sport</a>, play in <a href="/wiki/Championship_(rugby_league)" title="Championship (rugby league)">Co-Operative Championship One</a>. <a href="/wiki/East_Leeds_A.R.L.F.C." title="East Leeds A.R.L.F.C.">East Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oulton_Raiders" title="Oulton Raiders">Oulton Raiders</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/National_Conference_League" title="National Conference League">National Conference League</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bramley_Buffaloes" title="Bramley Buffaloes">Bramley Buffaloes</a> (previously <a href="/wiki/Bramley_RLFC" title="Bramley RLFC">Bramley</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Akkies" title="Leeds Akkies">Leeds Akkies</a> were members of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Conference" title="Rugby League Conference">Rugby League Conference</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Carnegie" title="Yorkshire Carnegie">Yorkshire Carnegie</a>, formerly known as <i>Leeds Tykes</i> and <i>Leeds Carnegie</i>, are the foremost <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> team in Leeds and they play at <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Stadium" title="Headingley Stadium">Headingley Carnegie Stadium</a>. They play in the <a href="/wiki/RFU_Championship" title="RFU Championship">RFU Championship</a> having been relegated from The Guinness Premiership at the end of the 2010\xe2\x80\x9311 season. <a href="/wiki/Otley_R.U.F.C." title="Otley R.U.F.C.">Otley R.U.F.C.</a> are a rugby union club based to the north of the city and compete in <a href="/wiki/National_League_2_North" title="National League 2 North">National League 2 North</a>, whilst <a href="/wiki/Morley_R.F.C." title="Morley R.F.C.">Morley R.F.C.</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Morley,_West_Yorkshire" title="Morley, West Yorkshire">Morley</a> currently play in <a href="/wiki/National_League_2_North" title="National League 2 North">National Division Three North</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Headingley" title="Headingley">Headingley</a> stadium is home to <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Yorkshire County Cricket Club">Yorkshire County Cricket Club</a> which is the most successful <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> team in England, with over 31 <a href="/wiki/County_Championship" title="County Championship">County Championship</a> wins. Their main rivals are <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_L.F.C." title="Leeds United L.F.C.">Leeds United L.F.C.</a> are the best-placed <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_association_football" title="Women&#39;s association football">women\'s football</a> team in Leeds, competing at the highest level <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_football_in_England" title="Women&#39;s football in England">in England</a>, the <a href="/wiki/FA_Women%27s_Premier_League_National_Division" title="FA Women&#39;s Premier League National Division">FA Women\'s Premier League National Division</a>. Leeds City Athletic Club competes in the <a href="/wiki/British_Athletics_League" title="British Athletics League">British Athletics League</a> and UK Women\'s League as well as the Northern Athletics League.\n</p><p>Leeds is home to a number of <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> clubs that compete in the <a href="/wiki/North_Hockey_Association" title="North Hockey Association">North Hockey League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Hockey_Association" title="Yorkshire Hockey Association">Yorkshire Hockey Association League</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Universities_and_Colleges_Sport" title="British Universities and Colleges Sport">BUCS leagues</a>. These include Leeds Hockey Club, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Adel_Carnegie_Hockey_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds Adel Carnegie Hockey Club">Leeds Adel Carnegie Hockey Club</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">University of Leeds</a> Hockey Club and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Beckett_University" title="Leeds Beckett University">Leeds Beckett University</a> Hockey Club.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\nLeeds Hockey Club Men\'s 1s gained promotion at the end of the 2016/2017 season to become Leeds\' first hockey team competing in a National League.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The City of Leeds Synchronised Swimming Club<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> train at the <a href="/wiki/John_Charles_Centre_for_Sport" title="John Charles Centre for Sport">John Charles Centre for Sport</a> and are represented by swimmers throughout the whole of the North East. The club was founded in 2008 and only compete in National and International Competition.\n</p><p>The city has a wealth of sports facilities including the <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a> football stadium, a host stadium during the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">1996 European Football Championship</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Stadium" title="Headingley Stadium">Headingley Carnegie Stadiums</a>, adjacent stadia world-famous for both <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> and the <a href="/wiki/John_Charles_Centre_for_Sport" title="John Charles Centre for Sport">John Charles Centre for Sport</a> with an <a href="/wiki/List_of_long_course_swimming_pools_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of long course swimming pools in the United Kingdom">Olympic-sized pool</a> in its Aquatics Centre<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> and includes a multi-use stadium. Other facilities include the Leeds Wall (climbing) and Yeadon Tarn sailing centre. In 1929 the first Ryder Cup of Golf to be held on British soil was competed for at the Moortown Golf club in Leeds and Wetherby has a <a href="/wiki/National_Hunt_racing" title="National Hunt racing">National Hunt</a> <a href="/wiki/Wetherby_Racecourse" title="Wetherby Racecourse">racecourse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> In the period 1928 to 1939 speedway racing was staged in Leeds on a track at the greyhound stadium known as Fullerton Park, adjacent to Elland Road. The track entered a team in the 1931 Northern league.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_Rhinos_vs._Salford_Red_Devils,_Headingley_Stadium_(21st_April_2014)_013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds Rhinos</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/2014_Tour_de_France" title="2014 Tour de France">2014 Tour de France</a> Grand D\xc3\xa9part took place from the Headrow in Leeds city centre on 5 July 2014.\n</p><p>Leeds is well known for its divers and features some of the best diving facilities in the UK. <i>City of Leeds Diving Club</i> who train at the <a href="/wiki/John_Charles_Centre_for_Sport" title="John Charles Centre for Sport">John Charles Centre for Sport</a> has trained many athletes who have competed at international and <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> level, with <a href="/wiki/Jack_Laugher" title="Jack Laugher">Jack Laugher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Mears_(diver)" title="Chris Mears (diver)">Chris Mears</a> making history by becoming the first ever divers from Great Britain to win an Olympic gold medal, a feat they accomplished at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Rio Olympics</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leeds_teams">Leeds teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Leeds teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table href="/wiki/Throstle_Nest" title="Throstle Nest">Throstle Nest</a> Stadium\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Pudsey" title="Pudsey">Pudsey</a>, Leeds\n</td>\n<td>1989\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds Rhinos</a>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> Rugby League\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Headingley_Stadium" title="Headingley Stadium">Headingley Stadium</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Headingley" title="Headingley">Headingley</a>, Leeds\n</td>\n<td>1870\n</td>\n<td>11\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hunslet_R.L.F.C." title="Hunslet R.L.F.C.">Hunslet</a>\n</th>\n<td><a Charles Centre for Sport</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hunslet" title="Hunslet">Hunslet</a>, Leeds.\n</td>\n<td>1883\n</td>\n<td>2\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Carnegie" title="Yorkshire Carnegie">Yorkshire Carnegie</a>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/RFU_Championship" title="RFU Championship">RFU Championship</a> Rugby Union\n</td>\n<td><a Leeds\n</td>\n<td>1991\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Yorkshire County Cricket Club">Yorkshire County Cricket Club</a>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/County_Championship" title="County Championship">County Championship</a> Cricket\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Headingley_Stadium" title="Headingley Stadium">Headingley Stadium</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Headingley" title="Headingley">Headingley</a>, Leeds\n</td>\n<td>1863\n</td>\n<td>33\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight: Basketball\n</td>\n<td><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carnegie_Sports_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carnegie Sports Centre (page does not exist)">Carnegie Sports Centre</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Beckett_Park" title="Beckett Park">Beckett Park</a>\n</td>\n<td>2006\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;">Leeds Hockey Club\n</th>\n<td>England Hockey Men\'s Conference North\n</td>\n<td>Sports Park Weetwood\n</td>\n<td>Headingley, Leeds\n</td>\n<td>1924\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_of_worship_in_the_City_of_Leeds" title="List of places of worship in the City of Leeds">List of places of worship in the City of Leeds</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Peter,_Leeds_(Leeds_Parish_Church)_(5373648288).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/St_Peter%2C_Leeds_%28Leeds_Parish_Church%29_%285373648288%29.jpg/220px-St_Peter%2C_Leeds_%28Leeds_Parish_Church%29_%285373648288%29.jpg" width="220" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/St_Peter%2C_Leeds_%28Leeds_Parish_Church%29_%285373648288%29.jpg/330px-St_Peter%2C_Leeds_%28Leeds_Parish_Church%29_%285373648288%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/St_Peter%2C_Leeds_%28Leeds_Parish_Church%29_%285373648288%29.jpg/440px-St_Peter%2C_Leeds_%28Leeds_Parish_Church%29_%285373648288%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2508" data-file-height="3270" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Peter,_Leeds_(Leeds_Parish_Church)_(5373648288).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Minster" title="Leeds Minster">Leeds Minster</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The majority of people in Leeds identify themselves as Christian.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_Data_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_Data-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Leeds does not have a <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> Cathedral: it is in the <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a> <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Diocese_of_Leeds" title="Anglican Diocese of Leeds">Diocese of Leeds</a> (formerly in the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Ripon_and_Leeds" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Ripon and Leeds">Diocese of Ripon and Leeds</a>), headed by the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Bishop_of_Leeds" title="Anglican Bishop of Leeds">Bishop of Leeds</a>, which has cathedrals in <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Cathedral" title="Bradford Cathedral">Bradford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ripon_Cathedral" title="Ripon Cathedral">Ripon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Cathedral" title="Wakefield Cathedral">Wakefield</a> although the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Ripon_and_Leeds" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Ripon and Leeds">Bishop</a>\'s residence has been in Leeds since 2008. The most important Anglican church is <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Minster" title="Leeds Minster">Leeds Minster</a>, although <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Church,_Leeds" title="St George&#39;s Church, Leeds">St. George\'s</a> has the largest congregation by far.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Leeds has a Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Cathedral" title="Leeds Cathedral">Cathedral</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bishop" title="Bishop">episcopal</a> seat of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Leeds" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Leeds">Roman Catholic Diocese of Leeds</a>. Many other Christian denominations and new religious movements are established in Leeds, including <a href="/wiki/Assemblies_of_God" title="Assemblies of God">Assemblies of God</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists_Together" title="Baptists Together">Baptist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Christ,_Scientist" title="Church of Christ, Scientist">Christian Scientist</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">Latter-day Saints</a> ("LDS" or "<a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormon</a>"), <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Christ" title="Community of Christ">Community of Christ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Army" title="Jesus Army">Jesus Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain" title="Methodist Church of Great Britain">Methodist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">Moravian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Nazarene" title="Church of the Nazarene">Nazarene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfrontiers" title="Newfrontiers">Newfrontiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Salvation_Army" title="The Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religious_Society_of_Friends" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious Society of Friends">Society of Friends ("Quakers")</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_Unitarian_and_Free_Christian_Churches" title="General Assembly of Unitarian and Free Christian Churches">Unitarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Reformed_Church" title="United Reformed Church">United Reformed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Vineyard_Churches" title="Association of Vineyard Churches">Vineyard</a>, an ecumenical Chinese church, <a href="/wiki/Living_Faith_Church_Worldwide" title="Living Faith Church Worldwide">Winners\' Chapel</a> and several independent churches.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SikhTempleLS7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large symmetrical two-storey building of yellow brick. The centre bay, incorporating the entrance, juts out. It has a large window with a semicircular top on the first floor and above is a golden onion dome on a blue base. At the ends of the frontage are hexagonal pilasters with small octagonal windowed pavilions and onion domes on top. Above the entrance is a white sign saying &quot;The Sikh Temple&quot; in blue. Each side has one two-storey and one one-storey window, and also yellow banners alongside the Temple&#39;s name. On each side of the entrance is a wooden seat, and strings of bunting are stretched across the scene." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/SikhTempleLS7.jpg/220px-SikhTempleLS7.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/SikhTempleLS7.jpg/330px-SikhTempleLS7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/SikhTempleLS7.jpg/440px-SikhTempleLS7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1930" data-file-height="1561" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SikhTempleLS7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sikh Temple, Chapeltown Road</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HarehillsMosqueDome.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/HarehillsMosqueDome.jpg/220px-HarehillsMosqueDome.jpg" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/HarehillsMosqueDome.jpg/330px-HarehillsMosqueDome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/HarehillsMosqueDome.jpg/440px-HarehillsMosqueDome.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1595" data-file-height="829" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HarehillsMosqueDome.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Harehills Mosque</div></div></div>\n<p>The proportion of <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> in Leeds is slightly above average for the country (5.4% as of 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-Census_Data_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_Data-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">Mosques</a> can be found throughout the city, serving Muslim communities in <a href="/wiki/Chapeltown,_Leeds" title="Chapeltown, Leeds">Chapeltown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harehills" title="Harehills">Harehills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_Leeds" title="Hyde Park, Leeds">Hyde Park</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Beeston,_Leeds" title="Beeston, Leeds">Beeston</a>. The largest mosque is <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Grand_Mosque" title="Leeds Grand Mosque">Leeds Grand Mosque</a> in Hyde Park.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikh</a> community is represented by <a href="/wiki/Gurdwara" title="Gurdwara">gurdwaras</a> (temples) spread across the city, the largest being in <a href="/wiki/Chapeltown,_Leeds" title="Chapeltown, Leeds">Chapeltown</a>. There is also a colourful religious annual procession, called the Nagar Kirtan, into <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Square,_Leeds" title="Millennium Square, Leeds">Millennium Square</a> in the city centre on 13\xe2\x80\x9314 April to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Vaisakhi" title="Vaisakhi">Vaisakhi</a>\xe2\x80\x94the Sikh New Year and the birth of the religion. It is estimated that around 3,000 Sikhs in Leeds take part in this annual event.\n</p><p>Leeds\' <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> community is the third-largest in the United Kingdom,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> after London and Greater Manchester. The areas of <a href="/wiki/Alwoodley" title="Alwoodley">Alwoodley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moortown,_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Moortown, West Yorkshire">Moortown</a> contain sizeable Jewish populations.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedman_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedman-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> There are eight active synagogues in Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> community in Leeds has a <a href="/wiki/Hindu_temple" title="Hindu temple">temple</a> (mandir) at <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_Leeds" title="Hyde Park, Leeds">Hyde Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> The temple has all the major Hindu deities and is dedicated to the Lord <a href="/wiki/Mahavira" title="Mahavira">Mahavira</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Various <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> traditions are represented in Leeds,<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> including: <a href="/wiki/Soka_Gakkai" title="Soka Gakkai">Soka Gakkai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism" title="Tibetan Buddhism">Tibetan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Triratna_Buddhist_Community" title="Triratna Buddhist Community">Triratna Buddhist Community</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zen" title="Zen">Zen</a>. The Buddhist community (<a href="/wiki/Sangha_(Buddhism)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sangha (Buddhism)">sangha</a>) comes together to celebrate the major festival of <a href="/wiki/Vesak" title="Vesak">Wesak</a> in May.\n</p><p>There is also a community of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_England" title="Bah\xc3\xa1&#39;\xc3\xad Faith in England">Bah\xc3\xa1\'\xc3\xad Faith</a> in Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Water supply and <a href="/wiki/Sewerage" title="Sewerage">sewerage</a> services in Leeds are provided by <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Water" title="Yorkshire Water">Yorkshire Water</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Kelda_Group" title="Kelda Group">Kelda Group</a>. Prior to 1973 it had been provided by the Leeds Corporation. Leeds City Council has a target of 11MW of renewable energy from onshore wind by 2010 and an aspirational target of 75MW by 2020. There are currently no operational wind farms in Leeds, but a planning application by <a href="/wiki/Banks_Group" title="Banks Group">Banks Renewables Ltd</a> for five turbines at Hook Moor near <a href="/wiki/Micklefield" title="Micklefield">Micklefield</a> was approved in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_central_library_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Leeds_central_library_001.jpg/220px-Leeds_central_library_001.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Leeds_central_library_001.jpg/330px-Leeds_central_library_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Leeds_central_library_001.jpg/440px-Leeds_central_library_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_central_library_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leeds Central Library.</div></div></div>\n<p>The area is policed by the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Police" title="West Yorkshire Police">West Yorkshire Police</a>. The force has five policing districts covering the West Yorkshire area, one of which covers Leeds. The Leeds District Headquarters is located at Elland Road in the South of the City. In the North West of the City the main stations are <a href="/wiki/Weetwood" title="Weetwood">Weetwood</a> and Woodhouse Lane; in the North East the main stations are Stainbeck near <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Allerton" title="Chapel Allerton">Chapel Allerton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Killingbeck" title="Killingbeck">Killingbeck</a>; in the South the main stations are Leeds Central located on Park Street in the city centre and the District Headquarters itself. Fire and rescue services are provided by the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="West Yorkshire Fire and Rescue Service">West Yorkshire Fire and Rescue Service</a>. The fire stations in Leeds are: <a href="/wiki/Cookridge" title="Cookridge">Cookridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gipton" title="Gipton">Gipton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunslet" title="Hunslet">Hunslet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanks" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanks">Stanks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moortown,_Leeds" title="Moortown, Leeds">Moortown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanningley" title="Stanningley">Stanningley</a> and the "Leeds" fire station (near city centre, on Kirkstall Road).\n</p><p>Health services are provided by the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Teaching_Hospitals_NHS_Trust" title="Leeds Teaching Hospitals NHS Trust">Leeds Teaching Hospitals NHS Trust</a>, Leeds Primary Care Trust<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> and Leeds and York Partnership NHS Foundation Trust<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> which provides mental health services. <a href="/wiki/Leeds_General_Infirmary" title="Leeds General Infirmary">Leeds General Infirmary</a> ("LGI") is a <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a> with more recent additions and is in the city centre. <a href="/wiki/St_James%27s_University_Hospital" title="St James&#39;s University Hospital">St James\'s University Hospital</a>, known locally as "Jimmy\'s"<sup id="cite_ref-St_James&#39;_Hospital/_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St_James&#39;_Hospital/-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> is to the north east of the city centre and is the largest teaching hospital in Europe. Other NHS hospitals are <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Allerton_Hospital" title="Chapel Allerton Hospital">Chapel Allerton Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seacroft_Hospital" title="Seacroft Hospital">Seacroft Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wharfedale_Hospital" title="Wharfedale Hospital">Wharfedale Hospital</a> in Otley, and Leeds Dental Institute. The new NHS Leeds Website provides information on NHS services in Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Joint_Services" title="West Yorkshire Joint Services">West Yorkshire Joint Services</a> provides analytical, archaeological, archives, ecology, materials testing and trading standards services in Leeds and the other four districts of West Yorkshire. It was created following the abolition of the county council in 1986 and expanded in 1997, and is funded by the five district councils, pro rata to their population. The Leeds site of the archives service is in the former public library at <a href="/wiki/Sheepscar" title="Sheepscar">Sheepscar</a>, Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Council" title="Leeds City Council">Leeds City Council</a> is responsible for over 50 public libraries across the whole city, including 5 mobile libraries. The main <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Central_Library" title="Leeds Central Library">Central Library</a> is located on the <a href="/wiki/Headrow" class="mw-redirect" title="Headrow">Headrow</a> in the city centre.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Leeds" title="List of people from Leeds">List of people from Leeds</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References_and_notes">References and notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: References and notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Max (City of Leeds) at SE140445 Hawksworth Moor in extreme west of district.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span
